Current Affairs Commentary

A Retrospective on the Thirtieth Anniversary of the Russo-Japanese War 38

— Ji

The Russo-Japanese War began on February 6, 1904. The Battle of Mukden (Liaoning) ended on March 10 of the following year. Japan, with a force of 350,000, drove the Russian army beyond North Manchuria, thus achieving final victory. In this war, the Japanese army suffered more than 40,000 casualties. The intensity of the battle and the magnitude of the sacrifice were unprecedented in Japan's foreign wars. In the blink of an eye, thirty years have passed.

The Japanese military, in order to recall the glory of their past victories and to encourage the people's outward expansionist sentiments, held a commemorative meeting today. They also published a booklet listing the stages of Japan's national power development, the world significance of the Russo-Japanese War, and the path to be taken in the future, thereby stimulating the Japanese people's awareness of the so-called extraordinary times. Looking back and ahead, we realize that the Russo-Japanese War was the beginning of determining the situation in East Asia today. Comparing China's current position and situation with that of thirty years ago, it seems that there is not much progress to speak of. What is past cannot be remedied, but what is to come can be pursued. Therefore, we present several points to inform the people of our country.

First, the location of the Russo-Japanese War was on Chinese territory, and the cause, beginning, and ultimate purpose of the war were also related to China. At that time, Japan, riding on the residual power of its victory over China, was ambitious for the Asian continent. However, its development towards the sea was blocked by the Imperial Russian fleet in the Far East, and its development on land was also hindered by the established forces of Imperial Russia in the South Manchuria area. In order to obtain its freedom of development in the East, Japan was determined to fight against Russia. Therefore, when the war broke out, the whole country was ecstatic, believing that the survival of the empire depended on this one action. The Japanese General Togo Heihachiro personally led the troops and commanded the battle. Finally, after a bloody battle of one year and three months, he destroyed the Russian power in the East. The firmness of their will to advance northward is worthy of our reflection, and their courageous spirit of resisting the enemy is indeed a model for us to emulate.

Second, after the war ended, the Japanese gradually began to manage Manchuria. They expanded the functions of the South Manchuria Railway Company, seized our northeast's railway construction and mine exploitation rights, and various other economic interests. Gradually, the Japanese were able to arbitrarily control things like immigration along the railway lines and police matters. Later, due to the maturity of economic and political aggression, the September 18th Incident occurred. The freezing of the dew into ice is by no means accidental. Examining historical facts, the beginning of this can be traced back to the Russo-Japanese War. The Japanese claim that the Russo-Japanese War and the Manchurian Incident have a consistent historical evolutionary significance and contain the value of transforming world history. This is indeed no exaggeration.

Third, after the Russo-Japanese War, Japan's national power expanded, and the pressure it exerted on China increased year by year. The revision of the Anglo-Japanese Alliance and the establishment of the Franco-Japanese secret agreement were all aimed at China. Japan actually controlled the activities of international financial groups in China. Moreover, the internal warlord wars in our country provided Japan with opportunities to exploit. During the European war, the pressure our country suffered became even deeper, and Japan's ambition to dominate East Asia flourished even more at this time, gradually becoming an unstoppable trend.

Fourth, Japan's attempt to dominate East Asia, although it suffered a considerable blow at the Washington Conference after the European War, the international relations in East Asia became even more complicated. Therefore, the competition of economic forces of the great powers in China and the invasion of our country's borders were not eased after the Washington Conference. Until today, the lost territory of our four northeastern provinces has not been recovered, and the situation of peace in East Asia is in imminent danger. Great calamities are coming, and there is no end in sight. How should we strive for self-reliance and save the crisis in the future? This is a question that the entire country, from top to bottom, should seriously reflect on today.

From the historical facts of the past thirty years, China and Japan have been in an unnatural relationship of oppression and being oppressed, whether in politics or economics. Is there any possibility for cooperation between China and Japan in the future? How should Japan change its attitude and means towards us in the past thirty years? If China and Japan cannot cooperate, what active preparations and sacrifices should we make to seek freedom and equality for China in the international community in the future? This is another question that we cannot help but raise to ask those who are paying attention to the issue of Sino-Japanese cooperation on the 30th anniversary of the Russo-Japanese War.

Page 7

Bulgaria's Understanding with Turkey; Balkan Situation Chaotic; Yugoslavia Issues Warning; Italy Declares Neutrality; League of Nations Secretary-General's Mediation 39

(London) The war clouds are slowly spreading over the Balkans, but reliable news is very scarce, so the current situation is very difficult to ascertain. Although the international panic caused by Turkey's troop build-up on the Bulgarian border has now subsided slightly, Yugoslavia is now in danger of being drawn into the vortex. According to news from Belgrade, the Yugoslav Foreign Ministry firmly believes that there is no danger of international disputes arising from this, saying that Bulgaria or Turkey will never have the reckless act of interfering in the Greek rebellion. However, if any foreign country interferes, the Balkan Pact will be implemented, and Yugoslavia will send troops to assist Greece and drive out the invading foreign troops. According to Reuters from Rome, the Italian authorities stated that Italy has not assisted the Greek rebels, nor has it encouraged Bulgaria to occupy an outlet to the Aegean Sea. Italy is completely neutral and has no contact with the Greek rebel leader Venizelos. According to news from Geneva, after the Turkish and Bulgarian representatives met this morning, Bulgaria withdrew the protest letter sent to the League of Nations opposing the Turkish troop build-up in Eastern Thrace. It is heard that direct negotiations will be conducted between the two countries to seek a peaceful resolution to this matter. (Reuters, 9th)

(Geneva) The matter of Bulgaria's application to the League of Nations yesterday seems to have been formally resolved today. When League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol met with the Bulgarian representative for the second time, he decided to regard Bulgaria's memorandum as a kind of information and distribute it to the members of the League of Nations Administrative Council for reference. If the Turkish government agrees, then Turkey's declaration will also be treated in the same way. Avenol then had successive talks with the Greek and Turkish representatives, and the result has eased the overall situation. (National Telegram, 8th)

(Geneva) People's minds in Europe have greatly eased today, as according to official news, the dispute between Bulgaria and Turkey has been resolved peacefully. However, the crisis of war has not completely dissipated. On the Greek side, more than 1,000 people have died in the civil war, and Turkey and Bulgaria are still stationed on the border with heavy troops, closely guarding. Bulgarian representative Antonov declared that the dispute has now been resolved, and that both Bulgaria and Turkey have expressed their willingness for peace to the League of Nations, and said that they now believe that Turkey's military actions on the border are not directed against Bulgaria. League of Nations observers said that this matter could easily have led to a major incident, and that the peaceful resolution this time was due to the exercise of pressure by the great powers. (National Telegram, 9th)

(Geneva) The Bulgarian representative to the League of Nations recently issued a declaration to the press, saying, "The memorandum of protest sent by Bulgaria to League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol on March 7 against the concentration of Turkish troops on the Bulgarian border should be regarded as 'not received,' because Bulgaria has received various necessary mitigation measures from all sides, and therefore believes that the memorandum of March 7 need not be submitted to the League of Nations Administrative Council." According to reports, Bulgaria's decision was the result of mutual explanations between the Bulgarian and Turkish representatives through the mediation of the League of Nations Secretary-General. Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu also issued a statement to the Bucharest Lador News Agency, saying that Bulgaria had no legitimate motive to submit a negotiation to the League of Nations, which is regrettable. He also said that in view of the current events in the Balkans, the unity of the signatory countries of the Balkan Consultative Pact is obvious. (Havas, 9th)

(Geneva) League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol met with Bulgarian representative Andonov today and explained that it was necessary for the country's memorandum to be sent to the Turkish representative for review. Once Turkey responds, the documents of the two countries will be submitted to the League of Nations Administrative Council for research. It is heard that Avenol believes that Bulgaria's sudden submission of a memorandum yesterday was unconventional and expressed this to Andonov. International figures here also believe that the Bulgarian delegation did not fully weigh the importance of the matter beforehand. This evening, Greek representative Rafael met with Avenol to explain that Bulgaria's military measures taken on the Greek border were not only unhelpful but also dangerous. (Havas, 8th)

(Rome) News from the Turkish capital states that the Balkan Pact countries, including Greece, Turkey, Yugoslavia, and Romania, are determined to limit any attempts to infringe on the territorial status quo of the Balkan Peninsula. Italian political figures believe that this is a warning to Bulgaria, so they are worried upon hearing the news, but they still firmly believe that countries like Turkey and Bulgaria are only strengthening their border defenses as a precautionary measure and have no other intentions. (Havas, 8th)

Greek Government Forces Prepare for General Offensive Against Rebels; Advance Thwarted Earlier by Snow 40

Salonika, Greece: Since this morning, the weather has begun to clear. Multiple government aircraft have flown to scout the positions of the rebel army. Minister of the Army Kondylis has gone to the Struma River front line to make the final preparations for the general offensive. It is likely that the general offensive will begin within a few hours. According to reliable news, the situation on the rebel side is becoming increasingly chaotic, and most of the rebels have surrendered to the government forces one after another. (Havas, 9th)

Athens: In the Greek civil war, it is heard that rebel leader Venizelos was injured and is now being transported to the port of Alexandria by destroyer. The government army's morale has been boosted by this news. Alexandria sources claim that if the rebel leader arrives here, the weapons on his ship will be disarmed and his guns will be temporarily detained. The war is still ongoing throughout Greece. Three government destroyers opened fire on Crete and bombarded the rebels in the Strymon Valley. It is heard that in the past few hours, the rebels have occupied the islands of Chios and Samos, while the central army has captured 700 rebels, 200 of whom are officers. (National Telegram, 9th)

Athens: A Yugoslav steamship in Volos intercepted a radio message saying that a famous Greek politician, Venizelos, had been seriously injured and transported to the port of Alexandria. If this news is confirmed, the rebels will be demoralized. Although the rebels have been attacked by the government army from the sea, land, and air, they remain stubborn and unsubdued. Yesterday, Greek Army Chief General Kondylis personally commanded the army to attack the rebels in Eastern Macedonia, but the heavy snow blocked the road, making it difficult for the government army to advance for a time. Therefore, 12 bombers bombarded the enemy's position. Kondylis is confident of victory, as the government army has 80,000 troops, while the rebels only have 6,000. It is heard that the rebels are suffering from a severe food shortage and are now looting villages. According to neutral sources, after fierce fighting between the two sides, Salonika was heavily bombed by the rebels. The five warships occupied by the rebels are now nowhere to be seen. It is heard that they have sailed to the vicinity of the island of Cyclades in the Aegean Sea. Four government warships have sailed out to prevent enemy ships from approaching the area within the firing range of Athens. Residents of the capital are fearful of being bombed by enemy ships and are moving to safer rural areas. The port of Piraeus in Athens is currently reinforcing its defenses day and night to prevent enemy ships from invading.

Greek Army Chief General Kondylis issued a communiqué stating that rain and snow were blocking the road and floods were rampant, causing the government army to fail to cross the Strymon River. The situation of the rebels is quite pitiful. Twenty aircraft dropped bombs on the enemy troops assembled in Serres. The local station was also the target of aerial bombardment. Aircraft reconnoitered the situation in Serres, and a large part of the area is now flooded. Greek Prime Minister Tsaldaris admitted today while meeting guests here that the government army was hindered by the severe weather and could not take advantage of the victory to advance, but said that the rebels would eventually collapse on their own. (Reuters, 9th)

Athens: The rebel fleet has recently concentrated in the port of Kavala in Macedonia, demanding that the Tsaldaris cabinet resign immediately and that rebel leader Venizelos form a government. Otherwise, they will open fire and bombard Athens. According to news from the Bulgarian capital, since last night, fierce fighting has been taking place between the rebel army and the government army 20 miles from the Bulgarian border. However, the Greek embassy in France issued a communiqué stating that "all private news should be treated with extreme reservation. Reports that the city of Larissa has been captured by the rebels and that the city of Salonika has been bombed by aircraft are completely unbelievable. The government army is now concentrated in the province of Macedonia, commanded by Minister of the Army Kondylis. He is now scouting the positions of the rebel army. Kondylis has expressed his desire to minimize bloodshed as much as possible. As for the friendly countries' sympathy for the legitimate Greek government and their hope that Greece will soon end the internal turmoil and consolidate peace in the Balkans, the Greek government is very grateful for this." The rebel warships "Hellas" and "Psara" have arrived at the port of Kavala, joining the rebel fleet there, and have occupied most of the islands in the Aegean Sea along the way. Kavala and Serres are centers of tobacco manufacturing. It is heard that the tobacco factory workers have formed a Soviet organization, with a tendency towards communism. Many senators and deputies of the city of Athens and former cabinet members such as General Tsavellasianos have been arrested, but they have been released after swearing to oppose the rebellion. Prime Minister Tsaldaris's wife has organized a Red Cross field hospital and is about to depart for Macedonia to treat wounded soldiers. Many young women have volunteered to serve as nurses. It is heard that Venizelos will declare independence in Crete and some islands in the Aegean Sea. (Havas, 8th)

London: General Plastiras, who was once the dictator of Greece for one day, is still residing in Milan. It is rumored that Plastiras has bribed several airlines with heavy money, planning to travel to Crete by plane, but this has been denied. It is heard that the Italian authorities have prohibited Plastiras from traveling to Greece from Italy, even if transportation is convenient. Regarding the news about the overall situation in Greece, there are many contradictions. The unrest has lasted for a week. According to observers, the fact that the rebels have been able to maintain their position for so long proves the strength of their power. The recent news from Athens about the rebels' danger cannot be fully believed. It is heard that the key at the moment is in the Aegean Sea. The warships occupied by the rebels can transport supporting comrades from various islands and ports on the mainland. According to today's communiqué from Salonika, the war in Macedonia cannot proceed due to unfavorable weather conditions. Government aircraft bombed the rebels' barracks and the Serres station today. The communiqué also denies the report that General Garstes, commander of the Komotini Division stationed in the province of Serres, has defected. The activities of the rebels are still unpredictable. It is believed that they have sufficient military pay and ammunition. (Reuters, 9th)

Great Powers Willing to Mediate in Greek Civil Strife; Prolonged War May Affect Trade 41

(London) It has been suggested that if the Greek government and the rebels voluntarily request the great powers to mediate, the great powers may as well mediate to bring the Greek turmoil to an early end. The British government has expressed its approval of this suggestion. According to political figures, the rebellion of former Greek Prime Minister Venizelos is entirely a matter of Greek internal affairs, and Britain does not want to interfere. However, Britain hopes for peace in the Balkan Peninsula and does not want it to be disturbed by this, so it is willing to do its best. However, Britain's actions should be absolutely limited to reconciliation. (Havas, 9th)

(London) Britain has a very large interest in the Near East, so the events in Greece are of great concern to Britain. People here believe that the government and the rebels are evenly matched, and the period of struggle may be prolonged. If that is the case, trade will inevitably be affected. It is also heard that the rebels may detain foreign ships, all of which make the British people feel uneasy. (Havas, 8th)

(Paris) The newspapers here are deeply concerned that the prolonged Greek civil strife may cause international turmoil in the Balkan Peninsula. The London correspondent of the Paris Echo declares that, as observed by Londoners, the situation in the Balkan Peninsula is extremely serious, and it is feared that the Bulgarian government is supporting the Greek rebels behind the scenes, while Turkey openly supports the Tsaldaris government, because the four countries of Greece, Turkey, Romania, and Yugoslavia signed the Balkan Consultative Pact in February of last year, jointly guaranteeing the territorial status quo of each signatory country. This pact was opposed by former Prime Minister Venizelos, and Bulgaria has always refused to join the pact. Le Petit Journal writes, "Venizelos's anger may have a serious impact on diplomacy and military affairs. The existence and effectiveness of the Balkan Consultative Pact have been proven by the Greek turmoil. The Turkish government has sent troops to Eastern Thrace because Bulgaria has stationed troops on the border, and its intention is to prove that the Balkan Pact and the various treaties previously signed between Turkey and Greece cannot be despised. Therefore, if the Greek turmoil lasts for a long time, or even if the rebels succeed, there is a possibility of extremely serious disturbances in this corner of Europe, which had previously been gradually returning to peace." The newspaper's correspondent in Bulgaria believes that there will be no disputes, saying that "Some clauses of the European war treaty are indeed not willingly adhered to by Bulgaria, but Bulgaria's rearmament in violation of the treaty is, at most, a defensive measure. The Bulgarian authorities have stated that the dispatch of troops to the border is a precautionary measure. In addition, the country's military strength is ultimately limited. Those who cry out loudly can be believed to have no other intentions." (Havas, 9th)

(Rome) The Italian cruiser "Brescia," the destroyer "Dario Mosto," and the "Pigafetta" have all been ordered to sail to the Italian-owned Dodecanese Islands in the eastern Mediterranean. People here believe that the Greek people are passionately patriotic. In this revolutionary turmoil, the country is divided into two halves, each unwilling to yield. There must be a fierce battle. As for Italy, it should maintain neutrality and never side with either party. When former Greek Prime Minister Venizelos was in power, he recognized Greece as a Mediterranean country and had good feelings towards Italy. Later, Greece joined the Balkan Consultative Pact, which Italy regretted. However, Italy maintains friendly relations with the current Greek government. The Italian government has advised former Greek dictator General Plastiras, who resides in Italy, not to use Italy's tolerant treatment to engage in political activities. Italy's friendly relations with the current Greek government can be proven by this. Moreover, Italy is currently negotiating with Abyssinia and has no time to take care of other matters, so Italy's only hope is for Greece to restore order as soon as possible. (Havas, 8th)

Italian Government Replies to German Explanation of Rome Accords 44

(Rome) Germany previously sent notes to the French and Italian governments, requesting detailed explanations of some of the proposals in the Franco-Italian Rome Accords of January 7. The Italian government has now sent a reply to German Ambassador to Italy Hassel, who will forward it to the German government. Although the contents of the reply are not fully known, it is generally believed that Germany requested explanations on two items. The first item asked how to interpret the so-called "agreement not to interfere in the internal affairs of the other country" in the Rome Accords. The Italian reply said, "According to the Franco-Italian Rome Accords, the signatory countries not only agree to respect other countries, especially Austria's independence and territorial integrity, but also agree not to take any actions that threaten the political and social system of the signatory countries." The second question raised by Germany asked whether other countries could also participate in the Danube River Convention in addition to the countries pointed out in the Rome Accords. The Italian reply said, "In principle, the Danube River Convention should first be signed by the countries that are directly connected by territory, namely Italy, Austria, Yugoslavia, Germany, Czechoslovakia, and Hungary. Later, Poland, France, and Romania may also participate in the convention." Finally, the Italian reply also provided detailed explanations of the League of Nations' role in implementing the Danube River Convention. (Havas, 8th)

Women in Soviet Industry 45

Leningrad: On "March 8" International Women's Day, newspapers pointed out that Soviet women are participating more and more actively in socialist construction. Now, materials on the participation of women in industry in Leningrad are presented, which are of great interest. In 1914, there were 76,413 women participating in industry in Petrograd. By 1934, this number had increased to 220,650, accounting for about 46 percent of all industrial workers in Leningrad. Women account for 13 percent of the local mechanical, technical, and scientific personnel. Before the revolution, one-third of the women in Petrograd were illiterate. Today, there are no illiterate women in Leningrad. (TASS, 8th)

Gan Meier Comments on China's Managed Currency System, Believing This System to Be a Stepping Stone to the Gold Standard, But Unsuitable for Chinese National Character 46

Princeton - Princeton University Professor Gan Meier, a world authority on currency systems, declared today that China's implementation of a managed currency system may lead to a form of gold standard. Because China has imposed heavy silver export taxes and promulgated other prohibitions on silver exports, it has effectively abolished the silver standard. The silver policies of the United States should be held responsible for this. If the United States abandons its silver policies in the future, the price of silver will inevitably fall, resulting in a large amount of idle silver stored in the U.S. treasury, which will affect the market. The situation will be similar to the re-entry of India's huge silver reserves into the market in recent years, disrupting the world silver market. Gan Meier also stated that the rise in silver prices due to the U.S. silver policy has increased the value of Chinese silver dollars, increasing the debt burden of the Chinese people and severely impacting China's export trade. Furthermore, if China continues to use the silver standard, its finances will be subject to silver purchasers with political influence, and ultimately to the U.S. government's sale of silver, which no country can tolerate. Therefore, the United States has effectively forced China to abandon the silver standard, but it has not considered that a managed currency system is unsuitable for China's needs and national character. China's adoption of this monetary standard is merely a stepping stone to adopting some form of gold standard. Professor Gan Meier's criticism has attracted attention from all sides, as Gan was an economic advisor to China several years ago and suggested that China adopt the gold standard. (8th National Telegram)

(Washington) Experts in Washington, after hearing that China plans to use foreign capital for a managed currency fund, declared today that approximately 100 million U.S. dollars are required to stabilize any new Chinese currency system. They also stated that China should have sufficient funds to offset several years of trade deficits. After China adopts a new currency system based on the British pound or U.S. dollar, trade deficits may cease. Reforming the currency system is indeed beneficial for China, as price levels can be stabilized when calculated in British pounds or U.S. dollars. As for current prices, they fluctuate with the price of silver. However, another view suggests that a managed currency system may require the large-scale issuance of paper money, which is a major difficulty because the Chinese people are not accustomed to using paper money. Moreover, paper money can be manipulated by political forces, which is also an obstacle to gaining the Chinese people's faith in a managed currency system. However, according to the opinion of most experts, although currency reform has many difficulties, it may be beneficial to China. (7th National Telegram)

(Hong Kong) According to the opinion of most bankers in Hong Kong, stabilizing China's currency is indeed a necessary plan, but it requires at least 100 million pounds. Regardless of the fixed exchange rate, currency stability is indeed beneficial for China. (8th National Telegram)

British, American, and French Stability of Financial Problems 47

(London) Sixty-three world economists, bankers, and business leaders, who attended the Carnegie Endowment Committee meeting here yesterday, passed many resolutions, the most important of which was to advocate that the governments of the United States, Britain, and France should immediately begin negotiations to restore the gold standard in order to achieve temporary international financial stability, with the aim of restoring the world gold standard. The committee also suggested that since Britain and the United States are leading creditor nations, they should immediately consult with each other and study with other governments how to enable debtor nations to repay their debts. The meeting lasted three days. Participants included Dr. Butler, President of Columbia University, Clay, Economic Advisor to the Bank of England, Chailan, Vice President of the National Bank of Belgium, and Trolenberg, Vice President of the German Chamber of Commerce, and other famous people. (9th National Telegram)

(London) Although the British government is currently maintaining its original position, refusing to hold negotiations in the near future to stabilize the currencies of various countries, some powerful figures in the financial community all hope to convene an international conference to jointly discuss and devise methods to cope with the consequences arising from the continued decline in currency values. The "Economist" weekly stated that although President Roosevelt cannot openly support international consultation on currency, debt, and tariff policies, now is the appropriate time to convene a second World Economic Conference in order to achieve results. However, before convening the meeting, it is essential that Britain and the United States fully agree on the main points. (8th Havas News Agency Telegram)

New York - Because France and Belgium advocate using gold to immediately convene a meeting to discuss the exchange market situation, people generally hold hope for currency stability. However, after British Chancellor Chamberlain stated yesterday that Britain is currently unable to stabilize the price of the pound in gold, this hope gradually faded. American observers are convinced that the U.S. authorities will not be swayed by the currency stability movement, but when necessary, President Roosevelt will naturally take the steps he considers best. Therefore, the United States will not refuse any movement that can improve the U.S. domestic economy. However, there is currently no event that can induce the United States to change its current policies, so changes are unlikely to occur in the short term. Today, the pressure on the British pound in the foreign exchange market seems to have temporarily disappeared. Both the U.S. dollar and the French franc are weak. The fluctuation of the British pound is relatively narrow, within two points. The closing price is $4.7875, up one and a half points from yesterday. According to London news, the London foreign exchange market felt mixed again today, but there were fewer transactions. News of unrest in the Balkans caused a buying spree of British pounds and short covering, so the prices of the U.S. dollar and the French franc rose compared to the British pound. Although the London gold price was listed at 148 shillings and 3.5 pence, the price fell by 1 shilling in the afternoon. (8th Reuters Telegram)

(Washington) The U.S. Treasury Department released today the amount of silver certificates and silver subsidiary coins in circulation within one month ending January 1 this year, with silver certificate circulation decreasing by 11 million U.S. dollars to 580,000,000 U.S. dollars, and silver subsidiary coins decreasing by 8 million U.S. dollars to 286,000,000 U.S. dollars. This is the first reduction since July of last year, and it is also a reduction of 155,000,000 U.S. dollars compared to the total amount of circulation in the previous month. Furthermore, the total amount of silver imported into the United States in the week ending March 1 this year was 3,054,000 U.S. dollars, an increase of 472,000 U.S. dollars from the previous week, of which 2,082,000 U.S. dollars came from England, and the rest came from Mexico 404,000 U.S. dollars, Canada 160,000 U.S. dollars, Peru 123,000 U.S. dollars, Chile 50,000 U.S. dollars, Argentina 127,000 U.S. dollars, Russia 18,000 U.S. dollars, the Philippines, Czechoslovakia, and Guatemala 3,000 U.S. dollars each, Yugoslavia 6,000 U.S. dollars, and Bolivia 1,000 U.S. dollars. (8th Reuters Telegram)

(London) In the week ending March 6, Britain's silver exports were worth £836,000 and imports were worth £226,000, so the net export value was £610,000. In the previous week, exports were worth £415,000 and imports were worth £412,000, with a net export value of £3,000. The United States shipped out the most, worth £818,000, and the remaining £18,000 was shipped to other countries. As for the sources of imports, India £34,000, African Gambia £88,000, Australia £61,000, Japan £22,000. (9th Reuters Telegram)

Commemoration of the Death of Sun Yat-sen, Peiping Party Department Holds Public Sacrifice at the Tomb of Clothing and Hats 62

Important Pending Issues Between Japan and the Soviet Union 88

(Japan Communication)

The negotiations between Japan and the Soviet Union, with their alternating periods of tension and relaxation, constitute a crisis in the Far East. Although this crisis has eased somewhat on the surface since the conference on the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway, there are still several important pending issues between Japan and the Soviet Union, such as: (1) the establishment of a Japan-Soviet-"Manchukuo" Border Committee; (2) the North Pacific fisheries dispute; (3) the oil exploitation rights in North Sakhalin; (4) the establishment of a demilitarized zone between the Soviet Union and "Manchukuo" and Japan's demand for the Soviet Union to withdraw its Far East forces. These are issues that deserve our attention. Of the above issues, the Soviet Union has agreed to the first, and the establishment of the committee will probably materialize soon. In the second issue, part of the problem, such as the exchange rate between the ruble and Japanese gold, has been largely resolved, with only the demarcation of fishing areas remaining problematic, but even that is likely to be resolved. However, the third and fourth issues will probably remain pending issues between Japan and the Soviet Union, and may even lead to unexpected disputes in the future. Now, please allow me to briefly report on the situation regarding these two issues.

Japan has recently been transforming from a highly developed light industrial country into a heavy industrial country. However, it particularly lacks the material conditions necessary for a heavy industrial country, especially oil. Its domestic production in 1933 accounted for only 7.8% of its total needs. Last year it was even less than that, and there are no areas that can be developed. The only relatively promising and geographically close option is North Sakhalin. However, the business performance of the Japanese there is poor, far less than the output of the Soviet state-owned oil wells. Furthermore, the lease for exploitation will expire next year. Even if the Soviet Union agrees to renew the lease for several years, Japan still does not have the confidence to achieve its expected results. In the future, if war breaks out, it will be even more difficult for Japan to control the oil mines there.

As for the establishment of a demilitarized zone, it is questionable whether the Soviet Union will agree. The Japanese military believes that this is inconsistent with Japan's national defense principles, because it is very difficult for the Japanese troops stationed along the Chinese Eastern Railway to withdraw. Therefore, it proposed another proposal, saying that the Soviet Union should withdraw the troops it has increased in the Far East back to their original defense and restore the border areas in the Far East to the situation before September 18th. In the past, the Soviet Union's Far East defense, from Chita to Vladivostok, had no more than 50,000 troops stationed there. The number of people included in the Pacific Division was not as large as it is now. Today, there are 200,000 Red Army troops stationed along the Amur-Ussuri Railway, with a strong air force attached, with about 600 aircraft, including 80 heavy bombers with a range of about 3,000 kilometers. These aircraft can not only threaten "Manchukuo", but also threaten major Japanese cities such as Tokyo, Osaka, Kyoto, and Nagoya. Vladivostok used to be an undefended seaport, but now it houses 40 submarines. Such defenses are definitely not without purpose. Although Japan uses diplomatic language to ask the Soviet Union to withdraw its defenses, will the Soviet Union agree? Moreover, Japan also has two large divisions, a flying regiment, and a tank regiment stationed on the Chinese Eastern Railway line. Which side will easily make concessions first? If concessions are made, where will reliable guarantees come from?

Japan sings the praises of peace, especially to maintain peace in the Far East, but Japan's national defense budget for 1935, including the army and navy, amounted to 1,021.1 million Japanese yen, which is larger than the average annual cost during the Russo-Japanese War. The tense situation in times of emergency is even more prevalent throughout Japan. The Soviet Union's defense expenditure has also increased from 5 billion rubles to 6.5 billion rubles, and the army has increased from 600,000 to 940,000. Neither side is willing to show weakness and both are planning for their own security, and both believe that only full armament can guarantee security.

Then, will the relationship between Japan and the Soviet Union become so tense due to facing each other with troops and excessive preparations that a war will break out in the future? Six months ago, it was impossible to guarantee. Now, the only cause of trouble in "Northern Manchuria," the Chinese Eastern Railway, will not lead to war, so at least in the short term, there will be no problems. The Soviet Union has always held the attitude of "We will not attack unless we are attacked." Of course, it will not take offensive measures at present. As for Japan, it has recently realized that invading Siberia will not bring benefits, and it is not sure to use force without reason, so it adopts diplomatic negotiations to achieve the goal of northward advance without using force. However, Japan's current situation is that it must still develop forward, and the continental policy must still be implemented. Therefore, the route it is now pursuing has turned westward and southward. This is what we cannot fail to pay attention to.

An Inspection Tour of the Northwest 90

—Special Correspondent Geng Ya

Xinjiang's Army and Education

During the era of Yang Zengxin, the Xinjiang army was poorly equipped, and rarely trained in peacetime. The quality was extremely simple. Later, when Jin Shuren managed Xinjiang, he tried to reorganize it, and purchased many new military weapons. After the April 12th coup, Sheng Shicai, the current Border Defense Commissioner, gradually eliminated political opponents such as Ma Zhongying and Zhang Peiyuan, and the provincial administration gradually became unified. He then took the opportunity to reorganize military affairs, reducing the brigades under his command, such as You Desheng, Meng Xu, Liang Qiwen, Song Qingling, and Shen Shiqi, into regiments. In addition to the original regiments, there were more than 20 infantry regiments and 9 cavalry regiments. The regiment was the organizational unit and was directly under the command of the Governor's Office. Other organizations such as artillery, engineers, aircraft, armored vehicles, and the Naturalized Army were also streamlining the old and weak and equipping them with new weapons and taxes. Today, the strength of the Xinjiang army is indeed not what it used to be.

The origin of the Naturalized Army: In the early years of the Republic of China, the Soviet Russian revolutionary cause gradually progressed. The royalist (White Russian) troops of Annenkov and Bachich, each with 8,000 to 9,000 troops and thousands of camels and horses, successively fled into Xinjiang, willing to surrender and naturalize. However, their intentions were unpredictable. Within three years, they caused incidents in Ashan Qitai and other places. They were mostly disarmed and dismissed by the provincial authorities and ordered to be stationed in various counties in northern Xinjiang, and a portion was sent into the customs. These were the so-called naturalized people. In the 20th year, the Hami Incident broke out. The provincial army was in urgent need of defense due to the emergency of the war. Therefore, more than 200 naturalized people were recalled and formed into two artillery special service companies, under the command of Zhang Peiyuan, the commander-in-chief of the front. They were surrounded by the forces of Hejia Niyazi in Liaodong and then released. It was rumored that the Naturalized Army had different intentions. Jin Shuren ordered them to be disarmed and dismissed to farming. In the spring of the 22nd year, Dihua was besieged. Jin Shuren once again gathered a regiment of the Naturalized Army, with Ba Pinggutai as the regimental commander. Later, the Naturalized Army participated in the April 12th coup and made meritorious service, and gradually expanded into a brigade. In the autumn of that year (22nd year), Tao, Li, Chen, and others contacted Ba Pinggutai and failed to overthrow Sheng. Sheng felt that Ba's subordinate Biekdiev had informed him, so he arrested Ba and promoted Bie to brigade commander. There were also Gui army officers Chechenov and Herovsky, who were promoted to brigade commanders in turn. In name, there were three Gui army brigades, but the actual number of people was still insufficient. In the spring of the 23rd year, Ma Zhongying retreated to southern Xinjiang, and the provincial army (including the Gui army) pursued them at every turn. Biekdiev was appointed commander-in-chief of the suppression of bandits in southern Xinjiang, with Wolek, the newly formed leader of the Ashan Gui army, as his deputy. Bie did not live up to the expectations of the people and was transferred to the front-line commander. The vacancy was filled by Liu Bin, the commissioner of the Ili Reclamation Area. Most of the Gui army is now stationed in Kashgar, and its combat effectiveness has always been stronger than that of other provincial armies.

In Xinjiang Province, one reason is that 60 to 70 percent of the population are Chantu, who do not understand the true meaning of education, and often obstruct the promotion of education. Another reason is that the authorities in the past lacked foresight and were perfunctory in running schools, and even implemented the Monroe Doctrine, so that books and newspapers could not be freely imported, resulting in cultural education being always behind. There are currently schools in the provincial capital, including the Russian Legal and Political College, middle school, and primary school. There is one Chantu school and one girls' school in each province and county. There are still many people in primary school, but above middle school, although subsidies are given, there are still few students. One or two primary schools have been set up in the outer counties, and the school name is still National Primary School, but most of them cannot be restored due to the closure of the war. Only the Chantu school run in Dihua has seen a booming trend in enrollment due to the appointment of Chantu people to important positions by the provincial government and the efforts of Cao Qiwen and others, the founders of the school. The leaders of the Chantu in several counties in southern Xinjiang also advocate their willingness to jointly run Chantu-Han combined schools with the government, so that their children can study and learn each other's Chantu and Chinese languages. In Aksu, Kashgar, and other places, the Chantu who serve in the military and political circles also send their children to study in Russia and Turkey. It is expected that the concept of Chantu education will soon change drastically. There is only one library for mass education in the provincial capital, and the books and newspapers on display are mostly old. There are two mass sports organizations, one is the Anti-Imperialist Association and the other is the Women's Association. The association is chaired by Qiu Yufang (Sheng Shicai's wife), the principal of the provincial girls' school, and Gu Lanshu (Zhang Xin's wife, the director of the Education Department), Chen Shumin (Chen Deli's sister, the director of the Finance Department), and Zheng Shuyuan. They advocate equal rights for women, women's education, marriage autonomy, and the liberation of concubines, and their work is very forceful.

Language and writing are the main tools of education. Xinjiang has a complex mix of ethnic groups, and their languages and writings are different. Every time a mass meeting is held in the provincial capital with the participation of all ethnic groups, a leader of one ethnic group must use several ethnic tongues to translate and narrate in turn, which is time-consuming and troublesome. It is conceivable that it is difficult for the effectiveness of education to be on par with that of the interior. It is not entirely due to poor human planning, but also due to objective conditions. However, comparatively speaking, among the languages and writings of various ethnic groups in Xinjiang, Chinese and Chantu are the easiest to circulate throughout Xinjiang. Official documents and announcements from government offices use a combination of Chinese and Chantu characters. It goes without saying that Chinese and Chantu people use Chinese and Chantu languages directly in civil and commercial communication. Other ethnic groups such as Mongolians and Kazakhs also mostly use Chinese and Chantu languages to express their meanings. Sometimes the influence of the Chantu language even exceeds that of Chinese. In areas where Chantu people gather in various counties, school education is certainly not developed, but private schools that study and recite the Muslim classics are everywhere. Therefore, if Xinjiang's education in the future still follows the old norms, only knows to implement unified general education, and does not seek variable special education, (such as adapting to the environment and trying to run Chinese-Chantu bilingual schools), it is feared that it will be counterproductive.

Page 9

The Five Provinces' Armies Surround Zhu and Mao's Remnants 91

The Defenses on Both Sides of the Wujiang River are Consolidated, and Xu's Bandits' Attempt to Flee to Gansu is Repelled.

Hankou Telegram: Zhu and Mao's remnant bandits retreated into Guizhou, intending to secretly cross the Wujiang River and join forces with He and Xiao's remnant bandits in western Hunan. At that time, President Chiang was stationed in Chongqing, and the morale of the bandit suppression armies was doubled. They pursued, suppressed, and intercepted them separately. Although the bandits were brave, it was difficult for them to fly across the Wujiang River. In western Hubei, Xu Yuanquan, the commander-in-chief of bandit suppression in the border area of the three provinces of Hubei, Hunan, and Sichuan, had taken office in Feng County, and He Jian, the commander-in-chief of the first route of pursuit and suppression, had also arrived in Changde to supervise the army and continue to encircle and suppress the two bandits, He and Xiao. It is reported that in the area of Meitan and Sinan, the army has been in contact with Zhu and Mao's bandits, and the elite of the bandits have been almost completely lost. Judging from the situation, it will be difficult to break through again. The bandits in southern Shaanxi, after failing to attack Nanbao, defended Ninggui on the one hand, and retreated to northern Sichuan with the rear team. Recently, there has been an attempt to flee to Gansu with all their nests. The Guojun troops were prepared to meet the attack at Dapanyu, Yaojiadu, and other places, killing thousands of bandits. It is expected that they will still be trapped in Nanjiang and make plans for the future. President Chiang, considering the tense military situation of bandit suppression, decided to sit in Chongqing temporarily and personally command all the bandit suppression military affairs in the three provinces of Sichuan, Yunnan, and Guizhou, in order to unify the steps of the various armies and achieve the full function of eliminating the bandits as soon as possible. Yang Yongtai, the Secretary-General of the Executive Headquarters, Chen Bulei, the first director of the Attendant Room, and He Chengjun, the Chief Pacification Officer stationed in Hubei, were all summoned to Chongqing to participate in the military affairs. Yang left Hankou by car on the 4th, passed Yichang on the 5th, passed Wanxian on the 7th, and will arrive in Chongqing on the 10th. He left by mail plane on the 8th and arrived on the same day. Chen is scheduled to take a boat west on the 9th with his secretary Chen Qiuyang. He told reporters on the verge of leaving that this time he was summoned to Sichuan to participate in the military affairs and would stay for a longer period of time. In the bandit suppression in Sichuan and Guizhou, our army has won consecutive victories and its prestige has been shaken. It is not difficult to wipe them out in one fell swoop. (8th)

The Xinsui Automobile Company, Responsible for the Important Transportation of Xinsui 92

From Suiyuan to Hami, It Can Be Reached in Ten Days.

Beijing Telegram: After the success of automobile transportation between Xinjiang and Suiyuan, the Xinsui Automobile Company is responsible for the transportation of Xinsui. According to Zhu Xiting, the general manager of the company, the organizational situation is as follows:

The Origin of the Founding of Xinsui Automobile

In the past few years, the commercial transportation between Sui and Xin was purely by camel. The two places only traveled back and forth once a year. If the road was slightly unstable, even a single trip back and forth was impossible. In addition, there were many obstacles along the way, which gave various inconveniences to commercial transportation. Once, dozens of merchants and camel households, in order to avoid excessive restrictions along the way, detoured through the Outer Mongolia route, (commonly known as the Great Grassland). As a result, all the camels of more than 2,000 heads and more than 4,000 loads of merchants' goods were detained by Outer Mongolia. After strenuous negotiations, only 200 to 300 camels and 400 to 500 pieces of goods were returned. The total loss was about 3 million yuan, which was the biggest fatal injury to Xinsui commerce. In the 18th and 19th years of the Republic of China, I (Zhu said himself) gathered comrades and traveled back and forth on the route several times by camel. After investigation, I decided to improve the transportation of goods in Xinsui and raised funds with Xinsui colleagues to establish Xinsui Long-Distance Automobile, which was the origin of the founding.

The Company's Share Capital is Expanded to One Million

The shareholders of the company are purely Xinsui merchants, hoping to cultivate this road with all their strength, as the lifeline of Xinsui commerce. Unexpectedly, after the establishment of the company, it encountered new changes and stagnated for more than a year. The original plan to use the income from the traffic as working capital also disappeared. However, during the stagnation period, the construction along the line was still not interrupted. In terms of economy, the old shareholders continued to add share capital and assumed the responsibility for working capital. Although the cars have been running recently, the construction along the way still needs to be added, and the amount of gasoline required is also considerable. It was decided to expand the share capital to 1 million yuan. Currently, 600,000 yuan has been fully collected, and the remainder is being raised. It is hoped that the government and those who are interested in the construction of the Northwest will provide assistance. Since the transportation of Xinsui is developed, the development of the future of the Northwest can be predicted.

The Number of Round-Trip Vehicles Will Increase in the Future.

There are currently only more than 50 vehicles traveling back and forth between Xinsui. In terms of the current commercial transportation situation, it is sufficient for application. In the future, new cars will be purchased at any time. According to past statistics, 80 cars were sufficient for the most prosperous year of Xinsui trade. As for the number of round trips, it was originally scheduled to run four times a month. Later, due to the new changes, commerce has not yet recovered, and there are not many merchants' goods, so the monthly trips are only once or twice. In terms of the current situation, the company has no profit. It is hoped that the situation will improve after the number of goods increases and the facilities along the way are completed.

Road Repair Projects are Implemented in Stages

Regarding road repairs, I (Zhu said himself) personally went to investigate. The ones that urgently need to be repaired now are Bailidun near Songshuling, which is about 70 to 80 miles long, and the soft sandy land near Juyanhai, which is about 300 miles long. They must be leveled separately. There are several small rivers between Bailingmiao and Heishatu, and bridges must also be built. The above projects are all large. We are actively trying to proceed. There are still many ups and downs in other places, which should be repaired at any time. It is now planned to handle it in three steps. The first step of the project will take about one year to complete. The road repair machines have been fixed in Shanghai and will be shipped next month, and will be implemented according to the plan. The road repair workers are required to be recruited in sections. The labor near Erlizihe in Juyanhai will be recruited from Jinta and Tiancang. The section from Suiyuan to Erlizihe will be recruited from Suiyuan. Those near Hami will be recruited in Hami. The branch line in Suzhou will be recruited in Suzhou. The food needed by the workers is transported by camel and stored in each station for backup.

Shorten Time and Develop Business

The route from Suiyuan to Hami is more than 5,000 miles long. At first, it took 20 days. Later, it was reduced to 16 days. After repeated reductions, it has recently been reduced to 10 days and even 8 and a half days. Although the standard for delay has not been determined, if the weather is good, the speed of the car will be more accurate. In the future, after the road repair plan is completed, it is expected to be reduced to one round trip every five days, which is incomparable to the past. The central government and the Sui and Xin authorities have previously promised to provide the company with material assistance. If it can be realized, the development will be faster. In addition to the postal agreement that the company has signed with the post office, it is currently negotiating a parcel agreement, which will be established soon. In this way, the company's business will have a reliable guarantee. As for the passenger fare, there was previously a preferential method for students, aimed at encouraging students in the Northwest to study in the interior. Recently, the company is very willing to treat the families of the righteous army going to Xinjiang with preferential treatment, but because of the large number of people, if it is handled in accordance with the preferential treatment method for students, the company will not be able to afford it. Assuming that it can afford the gasoline needed, the company can waive all other expenses. The difficulties in the middle are understandable to the people of the country. (7th)

Copper and Xiao Counties Jointly Dredge the Kui River 93

—Disputes Arising from Opposition by People of Su County Subside Quickly

Xuzhou Correspondence: Water conservancy in the Xuzhou region is underdeveloped, and river courses have long been neglected. As a result, farmland suffers whenever there is heavy rain. This spring, Copper and Xiao counties jointly dredged the Kui River, but the people of Su County in northern Anhui Province rose up in opposition, leading to disputes, which quickly subsided. The situation is described below:

Kui River Water Conservancy

The Kui River originates in the Shi Gou Lake southwest of Yuxu City, flows northeast through the Su Dike, passes between the east and west walls of the south gate of the city, then turns south, passing through Kui You, Sanguanmiao, Shilibu, Gaoying, Xusancun, Shilong Bridge, Huangqiao, Yiqiao, and Yangzhuang before entering Xiao County from Tong County. It then passes through Jiaqiao, Anlou, and Fenghuang Mountain in Xiao County before entering Su County, passing through Shixiangji and reaching Shicun, where it empties into the Sui River. The entire river is over seventy li long, with forty kilometers in Tong County, six kilometers in Xiao County, and thirty kilometers in Su County. Regarding its water conservancy relations, the water in the Shi Gou Lake at the source has dried up, while the water in the Jinzhong Lake south of Xing Mountain west of the lake overflows, pouring into the Kui River and increasing its source. South of Huangqiao, the Guanggou River also flows into the Kui River, and at Yiqiao, the Langxi River flows into the Kui River. There are no fewer than seven or eight other canals and ditches along the river that flow into the Kui River. Therefore, specifically in Tong County, the Kui River is related to the water conservancy of the east, west, and south sides of the county. In Xiao County, the water from Gushan Lake flows into the Kui River, and in Su County, it enters the Sui River, further increasing the water conservancy of the Sui River. The Sui River splits into three streams when it reaches Su County. The one north of the city is called the North Stream River, the one south of the city is called the Middle Stream River, and the one further south is called the South Stream River. The Kui River enters the North Stream River four li west of Shicun, which helps the Sui River for navigation and irrigation.

Reasons for Joint Dredging

The joint dredging by Copper and Xiao counties dates back to the joint dredging by Xiao and Su counties in the eighth year of the Republic [1919]. At that time, Xiao and Su counties were in contact, and the people of Su County believed that the Kui River flowed through the Phoenix Egg, where two mountains constricted the water. They feared that after dredging the upstream, the water flow would be too strong. They proposed diverting the river around the west side of the Phoenix Egg, with Xiao County helping. This was done once. However, after the people of Xiao County helped with the work, the people of Su County still interfered with Xiao County's dredging of the river. This time, the joint dredging by Copper and Xiao counties is a continuation of the previous agreement. The planned method is that Xiao County would start work on the third of this month and complete it in two weeks, while Copper County would start work on the eighth and complete it in one month. Xiao County would also inform Su County to start dredging at this time to improve water conservancy in the Xuzhou region and northern Anhui Province. This would thoroughly implement the previous agreement, and the Jinzhong, Guanggou, Langxi, and other rivers related to the Kui River in Copper County could all flow smoothly, and the Gushan and other water flows related to the Kui River in Xiao County would also benefit. The work began as scheduled after a report was submitted to the Commissioner's Office.

Course of the Conflict

After the people of Xiao County started work, the people of Su County gathered hundreds of armed militia and security teams at Shixiangji on the fourth. That evening, they crossed the border into Xiao County. Seeing that the people of Xiao County were dredging the river and concentrated at Anlou, they attacked Anlou. The people of Xiao County had expected this action by the people of Su County and were prepared, so they resisted. The two sides fought fiercely for a day and a night. On the evening of the fifth, the people of Su County, being isolated across the border and unable to withstand the military force, retreated to Su County. Both sides suffered injuries, but fortunately there were no deaths. After the people of Su County retreated, they remained gathered at Shixiang Town, while the people of Xiao County concentrated their defenses at Phoenix Mountain. Qu Zhuxun, the magistrate of Su County, rushed to Shixiangji and telegraphed Wang Gongyu, the magistrate of Tongshan County, asking him to relay to Yao Xuehuai, the magistrate of Xiao County, to meet at Phoenix Egg. After Wang relayed the message to Yao, both declined, saying that they had not received orders and could not leave the border. Yao then rushed to Anlou to supervise the work, while Wang also went to Yangzhuang on the morning of the seventh to prepare for work. Because the planned project between Copper and Xiao counties could not be stopped, it still needed to be continued.

Commissioner's Inspection

Shao Hanyuan, the commissioner of the Copper District, received a report of the conflict between the people of Xiao and Su counties, so he took the Jinpu train south on the morning of the seventh and got off at Caocun. At that time, Xiao County had sent a cavalry team to greet him. Shao rode to Jiaqiao and walked along the west bank of the Kui River to Anlou. Along the way, he saw that the people of Xiao County who were working, in addition to the able-bodied men, women and children were also participating. The people of Xuzhou's hardships were evident here. After arriving at Anlou, in addition to Magistrate Yao greeting him, Magistrate Wang also came to pay his respects. Shao carefully inspected the river work. The newly dredged river surface was about twenty meters wide, and the overturned soil was used to build the dikes, making the project very solid. Wang Niandong, the head of the Construction Department of Xiao County, was also supervising the work at Anlou. According to him, 30,000 laborers were currently employed, and it was originally planned to complete the dredging in two weeks, but now that the dredging had been accelerated, it could be completed in ten days. These 30,000 laborers were working hard under the protection of Phoenix Mountain, without any negligence, so that this project could be completed and other water flows could be dredged to solve the water conservancy problems of the entire territory. When Magistrate Wang came from Yangzhuang, he led many people from the townships to visit and learn from it, and after returning, he would start work the next day (the eighth). Yao reported to Shao the situation of the conflict at that time. Shao instructed that since the conflict was over, no more quarrels should be started. He should complete the Kui dredging project while taking a peaceful negotiation attitude under legitimate defense. After inspecting the sections, Shao returned to Caocun and took the Jinpu evening train back to Xuzhou. After the people of Su County returned to Shixiangji, most of them had dispersed, but 200 members of the security team were stationed there, and the turmoil could be expected to subside. Qu Zhuxun, the magistrate of Su County, came to Xuzhou from Su County on the evening of the seventh. After inquiring and learning that Commissioner Wang and Magistrate Yao had both gone to Anlou and could not meet, he returned to Su County. It is estimated that this matter can be resolved peacefully.

Project Plan

The Kui River flows the most through Copper County. The Construction Department of the County Government measured and marked the route, with one marker every 300 meters. The width of the new river bottom was 4 meters at marker zero, and increased by 6.9 centimeters per marker thereafter. At marker 23, the Chenghai River flowed in, adding 2 meters in width. At marker 97, the Guanggou River flowed in, adding 3 meters in width. At marker 112, the Langxi River flowed in, adding 2 meters in width. At marker 131, the end point of Copper County, the bottom width was 20 meters. The slope of the river bottom was divided into three sections: 1 in 2500 from marker zero to marker 17 (Su Dike), 1 in 5000 from marker 17 to marker 35 (Kui Mountain), and 1 in 8000 from marker 35 to marker 131 (Jiaqiao). The slope was 1:1 except for the areas near the city, where it was 1:1.5. The total earthwork was 960,000 cubic meters, and it was estimated that 10,000 laborers could complete it in one month. The river work in Xiao County was similar to the end point of Copper County, and the project could be completed in ten days. As of today (the eighth), it is already halfway completed. (the eighth)

Jiaoji Railway Bureau Holds Discussion Meeting on Improving Commercial Transport 94

Over one hundred representatives from various places attended, with over one hundred proposals presented. Qingdao Correspondence: The Jiaoji Railway convened a discussion meeting on improving commercial transport. Preparations had been made for many days in advance, and chambers of commerce along the line were notified to send representatives to Qingdao to participate. The Railway Bureau received over one hundred proposals from various places, and the representatives from various places have now arrived. At 10:00 am on the sixth, after the representatives signed in, the opening ceremony was held in the bureau's auditorium. Attendees included Zhang Honglie, the Director of the Shandong Construction Department; Shen Honglie, the Mayor of Qingdao; Chu Zhen, the Director of the Social Affairs Bureau (representing Dong Zhidao); Ge Guangting, the Chairman of the Jiaoji Railway Committee; Lu Mengxiong, Cui Shijie, Peng Dongyuan, Chen Yanwen, Tan Shukuai, the Director of the Military Affairs Department, and others. After the meeting began as scheduled, Chairman Ge Guangting delivered the opening speech, saying, "Today, the Jiaoji Railway's discussion meeting on improving commercial transport is being held. We are honored to have representatives from various places participating from afar, and to have Director Zhang of the Provincial Government, Mayor Shen of this city, and distinguished guests attending. Railway transport and commercial trade are as interdependent as the spokes of a wheel. The prosperity or decline of transport and the rise or fall of commerce are mutually dependent and closely related. Therefore, if we want to develop the railway and prosper commerce, we must have cooperation and assistance between the railway and businesses to be effective. I have been in charge of this railway for four years, and all the measures taken have been in line with the principle of mutual assistance between the railway and businesses. I have done my best to accommodate and strive for this goal. For example, I have repeatedly submitted proposals to the Ministry of Railways for approval to reduce freight rates for coal and major agricultural products, which are clear examples. Therefore, in recent years, even in the midst of the national economic depression, businesses along the line have generally benefited from considerable convenience, and the railway's transport has also increased slightly. This is the result of the sincere mutual assistance between the railway and businesses, which I am proud to report. However, in recent years, due to the impact of various environments, the changes in the commercial sector have been rapid. The rise and fall of commerce in various places, the increase and decrease in the production of goods, the urgency of needs, and the ebb and flow of sales have all undergone changes. Therefore, how can we ensure that the railway and businesses can meet each other's supply and demand and work together seamlessly? Only by the railway and businesses re-discussing and coordinating plans can we adapt to the times and jointly devise improvements. The railway, in view of this, has organized this improvement discussion meeting. We hope that the representatives will uphold the spirit of mutual assistance from the past, be open and honest, and conduct detailed discussions to arrive at a common conclusion. Within the possible scope, the railway will do its best to implement them to meet your expectations. Furthermore, since the 21st year of the Republic [1932], the production and sales of coal and major agricultural products in Shandong Province have been affected by various factors and have not been prosperous. Fortunately, Director Zhang of the Shandong Provincial Government and Mayor Shen of this city, as well as the Port Authority, the Social Affairs Bureau, the China Merchants Bureau, and various legal entities, have provided many protections and unanimously appealed, and last year there was a great improvement. To seek the welfare of commerce, I sincerely hope that Mayor Shen, Director Zhang, and all parties will express their views and guide the railway and businesses to cooperate so that we can follow their guidance. This is what I earnestly hope for." Next, the Director of the Traffic Department gave a report, saying, "The meaning of convening this discussion meeting on improving commercial transport has already been reported by the Chairman. Now, I will briefly report to you on the recent measures and improvements in traffic management. The main freight of this railway is coal, coke, peanuts, tobacco, and cotton, followed by wood, flour, wheat, cotton yarn, soybeans, and raw beef. Last year, the total transport volume was about 4.33 million tons, an increase of one time compared to the total transport volume of 2.44 million tons in the 18th year of the Republic [1929]. The reason why we were able to achieve this result is entirely due to the cooperation between the railway and businesses. The improvements in passenger and freight transport in the past and the distribution of vehicles are described below. (1) Passenger Transport: The improvements in passenger transport can be divided into twenty items: 1. Adding second-class sleeping cars; 2. Renovating first-class sleeping cars; 3. Renovating the seats in third-class passenger cars to make passengers more comfortable; 4. Adding arrival announcement systems to passenger trains; 5. Posting safety posters in stations; 6. Paying attention to cleanliness inside the cars; 7. Improving the dining car service to make it more affordable and building a railway hotel at Weixian Station; 8. Adding waiting rooms at each station; 9. Increasing or extending the platforms at each station; 10. Building rain shelters at major stations; 11. Extending ticket sales hours; 12. Adding passenger information desks; 13. Adding refrigerated cars; 14. Expanding passenger intermodal stations; 15. Organizing water-land intermodal transport; 16. Planning automobile intermodal transport; 17. Planning to open a Qingping direct train; 18. Extending the summer tour ticket time; 19. Adding second-class sleeping cars for group tours to Qingdao from Pingjin and other places; 20. Shortening daytime driving time. (2) Freight Transport: The improvements in freight transport can also be divided into twenty items: 1. Expanding the scope of responsible transport; 2. Organizing domestic intermodal transport; 3. Organizing water-land intermodal transport; 4. Implementing through transport between Luo and Huang; 5. Implementing railway collection of freight charges; 6. Issuing railway freight pickup cards; 7. Providing low-cost freight insurance; 8. Reducing freight rates for bulk goods; 9. Organizing economic surveys along the line; 10. Formulating special prices for intermodal goods; 11. Cooperating with academic institutions to improve agricultural products; 12. Adding or extending freight platforms at each station; 13. Adding freight houses and food storage at each station; 14. Adding sidings at each station; 15. Adding ninety-ton shunting engines; 16. Building shunting yards at Dagang and Zhangdian stations; 17. Increasing locomotives and rolling stock; 18. Increasing freight car accessories; 19. Shortening the time for freight handling; 20. Extending the summer freight car detention time. As for the railway's distribution of vehicles, it has always been based on the principle of fairness and impartiality for various commercial goods on trunk and branch lines. The railway's freight sources usually come from coal and coke from stations on the branch lines, local products from Jinan, and imported groceries from Qingdao. In terms of transport, more goods come from the east than from the west, with the west accounting for only half of the east. In the past, due to frequent military operations, many of the railway's freight cars were requisitioned. As of the end of the 18th year of the Republic [1929], more than 300 cars (more than 6,000 tons) had not been returned, accounting for one-sixth of the railway's original freight cars. Later, the railway successively purchased 150 coal cars and 50 covered cars of 40 tons each, totaling 8,000 tons, which restored the old appearance of the loss of transit vehicles. It is estimated that the total number of vehicles on the railway is more than 41,000 tons. Excluding the transit vehicles that have not been returned and those that are routinely repaired in the factory, the total number of vehicles that can be used is more than 35,200 tons. If calculated at an average turnover of once every three days, the daily practical loading capacity is about 10,000 tons. Therefore, it is difficult to cope with the busy freight transport in winter. Regarding the distribution of trains on the branch lines, the station is the unit first, and then the coal merchant is the unit for distribution. The method of allocating vehicles to each station is to allocate them according to a certain ratio. This ratio is determined based on the annual coal transportation volume of each station. Boshan accounts for 51%, Hongshan accounts for 27%, and Dakunlun accounts for 22%. The total number of coal trucks allocated to branch lines in the past three years has increased year by year. It is estimated that the number of vehicles allocated in the 22nd year of the Republic [1933] increased by about one-fifth compared with the 21st year of the Republic [1932], and the number of vehicles allocated in the 23rd year of the Republic [1934] increased by more than one-fifth compared with the 22nd year of the Republic [1933]. This is due to the gradual increase in coal and coke transportation and sales, and the acceleration of vehicle turnover can also be seen. The tonnage loaded on the trunk line is usually more than 4,000 tons per day, and can reach 5,000 to 6,000 tons during peak periods. Combined with the tonnage of freight transported on the branch lines, the daily average is about 10,000 tons. Based on the above, the railway's daily practical loading capacity can only cope with the continuous transport, and it is difficult to have a sudden increase. If the transportation of bulk goods is booming and it is desired to fully transport a certain kind of goods, it is not possible. In addition, the demand for vehicles from merchants at various stations often increases or decreases with the rise and fall of market prices, that is, they are eager to clear the goods when the market price rises, and they hoard and wait and see when the market price falls, failing to continue average consignment, resulting in the supply and demand often failing to correspond, which is what the railway feels most difficult about and hopes to improve together. In total, the freight transport performance in the past six years has increased year by year, except for the 19th year of the Republic [1930] when the route was interrupted due to the war, resulting in a reduction in color due to the suspension of transportation for two months, and the most significant increase was in the 23rd year of the Republic [1934], which was 49% more than in the 18th year of the Republic [1929]. This is proof that the performance of dispatching has increased year by year." Then Mayor Shen, Director Zhang, and Commissioner Lu gave speeches, and finally the Chairman gave a reply. It was already past 12 o'clock, and the meeting adjourned after taking pictures. The meeting is scheduled for two days, so the meeting will continue on the afternoon of the sixth and tomorrow (the seventh) to discuss the proposals of various industries. (the sixth)

Songjiang North Suburb Jiangbei Shantytown Fire 95

The Yanghua Bridge area outside the north gate of this city is a gathering place for Jiangbei people who travel to Songjiang. They each built shanties to live in, and make a living by operating small businesses and manual labor. Unfortunately, at 4 pm on the ninth, there was a fire in the shanties, which was not guarded against. The wind was high and the air was crisp, and the fire spread very quickly. By the time the alarm was raised and fire trucks from various districts rushed to the scene, the fire was raging everywhere and could not be approached. After hard work and pouring water, the fire was finally extinguished. A total of thirty-seven rooms were burned down. Fortunately, no one was injured, which is truly a great calamity for the traveling people of Songjiang.

Rifeng Robbery Criminal Sentenced to Seven Years 96

The Rifeng Silver Building in the city was robbed one morning last winter, losing a pair of gold bracelets. Zhao Houzhuang, the manager, was shot and wounded. That day, the water patrol team captured a young robber named Zhao Zhiyi and a pistol marked with the words "Shanghai Public Security Bureau." Under interrogation, he confessed without hesitation. At that time, local groups were worried and uneasy because the winter defense had begun and there was a robbery and injury during the day. They telegraphed the province requesting severe punishment. The county government also telegraphed the province for instructions based on the confession. It was ordered to send him to the judicial department for interrogation. After investigation by the prosecutor's office of the county court, a public prosecution was filed. The defendant, Zhao Zhiyi, hired a lawyer, Shou Yi, to defend him. The details of the final defense have been recorded in this newspaper. It is now learned that the court announced the sentence today. Zhao Zhiyi was sentenced to seven years in prison for the crime of robbery. The case of the daytime robbery in the city, which was watched by the public, has come to an end.
