Women's Corner

Case of Western Police Officer Beating a Vegetable Vendor to Death 193

— Wen

The China Daily reported on the 7th of this month: "Zhao Liujia, a woman from Shanghai, was selling vegetables on Yichang Road the other day when she was interfered with and brutally beaten by English Western Police Officer No. 62 from the Putuo Road police station, resulting in her death. All sectors of the city are quite indignant about this incident. The Citizens' Federation organized the Zhao Woman Disaster Relief Association at 4 PM yesterday... to conduct negotiations and ensure that the goals of punishing the perpetrator and providing compensation are achieved."

I remember a similar news item a year or two ago: "A lacquerer, Liu Mingshan, was enjoying the cool with friends at the Dagu Wharf when he was suddenly kicked into the water by a Russian police officer, but the Russian police officer said that the lacquerer had accidentally fallen into the water."

In fact, on the Shanghai Bund, the Second Heads and Third Heads bestow small favors—kicks, punches, sticks—on rickshaw pullers, vendors, and coolies; the rickshaw pullers, vendors, and coolies who suffer these indignities not only dare not resist, but also have to kowtow and pray for the foreign lords to forgive them. This is already commonplace and not considered a big deal. However, things did not go as planned: the lacquerer Liu Mingshan "would accidentally fall into the water," and the vegetable vendor Zhao Liujia "would trip over a stone, bleed to death" (according to Police Chief Martin—see the 6th of this newspaper). In reality, everyone knows that the former was given a bath and the latter was knocked down with a club. This is too stimulating. Even people who are used to these tricks will be moved. The lacquerer's matter has passed and will not be discussed, but the Zhao Woman Disaster Relief Association has been organized. We hope to achieve the above goals, and we especially hope that women's groups in this city will rise up to respond to this relief association.

Punishing the perpetrator and providing compensation, even if it can be done, is already turning a big thing into a small thing, because this is not Zhao Woman's personal grievance, but a disgrace to the entire nation! Bai Shi

Mourning Ruan Lingyu 194

— Bai Shi

While the women's organizations of Shanghai were grandly commemorating the "March 8th" International Women's Day in various halls with fragrant flowers, elegant clothes, joyful conversations, and clear singing, Ms. Ruan Lingyu, the most famous movie star in the film industry, had just taken sleeping pills and was moaning and groaning in the hospital. This is so discordant—of course, the news of women's suicides these days can compete with the lush spring grass; however, because of the shameless pursuit by male brutes, even a big star with a promising future and economic security had to take the path of death. The social significance contained in this seems even deeper.

Some time ago, I read Ms. Ruan's marriage lawsuit, which was enough to make people sick and heartbroken. A woman who ends a cohabitation relationship with a young master still has to pay him a monthly allowance of one hundred yuan; and even after the two-year period has expired, there are still unexpected entanglements. This young master, who occupied Ruan Lingyu's first half of her life with the advantage of money, thought that Ruan Lingyu was his possession, the pearl in his palm; that past cohabitation relationship had permanently tied Ruan Lingyu down for life. How absurd! And the public did not sanction that absurd worm, but instead gave Ruan Lingyu a cold and cruel stimulus. How absurd is this society!

In the true feudal era, there were no men who shamelessly begged women for living expenses. In the true capitalist era, men could ask women for money, but they did not dare to force them through a divorced cohabitation relationship. Only in this era can a divorced man still be allowed to have a reason to preserve his husband's rights, and can he be allowed to be forgiven for begging women for money. This is truly an unnameable and monstrous era!

Even though the era is monstrous, men, while maintaining their capitalist society's monetary advantage of male power, also add the male power of feudal consciousness dug out from the grave to oppress weak women; women have nowhere to escape, escaping into the hell of the ghost world to avoid the hell of the human world. But in the eyes of imperialists, what do men who exert authority over women become?

The monstrous era kills weak women more and more every day and builds a male-centered world more and more every day. We know that the earth is about to sink!

Ms. Ruan Lingyu came from a humble background. Although she has outstanding artistry in the film industry, she is still not "crowned" as queen. Unexpectedly, in addition to her many troubles, she was also forced by brutes day and night, causing her to abandon art and abandon life. Can female compatriots under double oppression not cry out in unison?

How Do We Understand Literature and Art? 195

— Qin Chuanbi

I cannot elaborate on profound theories here, nor do I intend to encourage many girlfriends to strive to become writers and artists. I simply feel that we should have a correct appreciation of the novels, songs, paintings, music, movies, dramas, etc., that we often encounter in life. Therefore, I would like to propose a preliminary discussion.

In a society where many careers do not allow women to participate, the arts seem to be relatively open to women. Feudal society wanted women to engage in embroidery, poetry, painting, and music because these things could entertain men and cultivate women's gentle temperament. Poetry taught women to be melancholic and sickly, comparing women to flowers and birds, and using all sorts of insulting nouns and adjectives to describe them. At the time, unaware women appreciated and imitated this kind of literature and art, and took pride in it. Most of the artistic fields in the male-centered feudal era originated from this kind of consciousness, and their function naturally lay in creating women's "weakness" and "媚物." Women in capitalist society are no longer willing to lurk in their families. They want to fight for equality and freedom; but the rulers of the bourgeoisie still want to lock them back in their homes, to cut off all their connections with society. In addition to restricting women in politics, law, occupation, and education, they advocate that women should use literature and art as a toy to cultivate their character and pass the time, and falsely claim that women are naturally close to literature and art. This is, of course, an attempt to make women fascinated by literature and art and abandon all due social responsibilities. Therefore, under the rule of the bourgeoisie, poor women are certainly not educated and are forever out of touch with proper literature and art; intellectual women also cannot have proper appreciation because of misunderstandings of art. As for the general noblewomen, of course, they can only receive some obscene and vulgar so-called works of art to satisfy their麻醉欲as媚物.

Now, women's lives are gradually changing with the changes of the times; we want to have direct relations with all aspects of society with the qualification of "people." In the new society, art is not a toy, it is not for people to cultivate their character or pass the time, and we can no longer inherit others' use of it as a tool to fool women. We demand a correct understanding of literature and art.

First of all, we must understand that art is the superstructure of society, and it reflects the basic organization of society at all times. In the feudal era, men ruled the entire society with the heroic postures of lords, nobles, generals, and emperors, so there were poems singing the praises of male heroes, dramas rewarding virtuous women and martyrs, and legends depicting "talented scholars and beautiful women" and "love affairs between sons and daughters." These kinds of works of art represent the central consciousness of the society at that time. It is very possible to produce extremely high-level masterpieces, which not only made people sing and weep at the time, but also can still move people's hearts and show the power of art when they are passed down to later generations. However, when these works of art are placed before us, we must know how to understand them with the eyes of modern people—that is, standing on the position of today's society; we should not follow the ancients to sing, weep, worry, and rejoice as if we were realistic social persons. When we read "Palace Lament," "Boudoir Lament," and countless poems of sexual love, we must recognize from them how feudal women were sacrificed to men, and what kind of weak, deceptively weak, charming, and playful things women are in the minds of men; do not be fascinated by those lingering and secluded resentments, and make yourself so neurasthenic. Reading "Dream of the Red Chamber" requires recognizing that it is a history book of a feudal family, to discover the darkness of the feudal family and the pitifulness and shame of so many women; and to strictly prevent yourself from becoming "Lin Daiyu-ized." Facing the old plays, we must recognize from the stories of those virtuous women and martyrs the methods by which men have been trying to win over women for thousands of years, the viciousness of women, and the tragic history of women's lives with blood and tears for thousands of years. If, after watching "Farewell My Concubine," you openly sympathize and praise the hero and the beauty, then you have been poisoned by feudal art. Treating art with true interest will inevitably be an unrewarding surrender at the foot of art.

At present, we live in an artistic environment of the remnants of Chinese feudal art and the imported bourgeois art of Europe and the United States. Urban personnel listen to the broadcasting of old operas and Suzhou ballads every day, and see the advertisements of foreign movies every day. We are not saying that these works of art should never be appreciated; on the contrary, we should pay more attention to giving them a serious understanding and criticism. The novels and dramas of 19th-century European and American realism and naturalism played a very great task in exposing the sins of capitalism; we should strive to appreciate and identify them. In the works of all famous great writers, there are extremely erroneous views, and there are also many histories that are more accurate than history textbooks. The works of Tolstoy, Turgenev, Balzac, Zola, Maupassant, Ibsen, and Shaw almost help you understand the shape of modern European life more than any other book. In the last ten years of the 20th century, film has become one of the most powerful urban education tools; almost all citizens are directly and indirectly affected by it. "How should we appreciate movies?" is really a topic that modern citizens should have. In particular, there are the most performances of all aspects of women's lives, and we should pay attention to how modern bourgeois film, the most powerful art, educates bourgeois women in obscene decorations and expressions, and how to confuse men; at the same time, how bourgeois men wantonly play with women. —Unreasonable social systems create unreasonable gender relations, and unreasonable gender relations create so much sin and pain; perhaps only movies provide us with so many rich and vivid materials! It is difficult to find correct life guidance in bourgeois artistic products; but when we appreciate them with the belief of exposing ugliness and criticizing mistakes, we can learn something. Many people say that watching movies is just for entertainment, why bother demanding any theoretical problems. This is committing the mistake of separating entertainment from life. People's knowledge, sentiments, consciousness, and living habits are greatly influenced by their usual entertainment; entertainment is education. Drinking poisonous wine from a cup of entertainment will still make people mad and die.

Society is moving forward, and the emerging art is also raising its head and growing. It is gradually possible to seek from the art representing the era an explanation of society and guidance for life. What kind of novels, songs, dramas, movies, etc., can be considered good works of art today? Now is not the time to explore profound theories, but we can try to give readers some basic standards. First, only reality is the yardstick for measuring art; it is meaningless to advertise for the dead ancient times or to ask questions about unfounded fantasies.

Second, we must use the most common facts as the subject matter of typical things. In this world and country of famine and suffering, abandoning the lives of the vast masses and specializing in the jokes and love affairs of the rich and idle is not what we need.

Third, perhaps it is a description of ancient historical facts, perhaps it is a record of the lives of the rich and idle, but its purpose is to help understand the modern world and to expose the work for the masses. That is proper and necessary.

Fourth, if the language that makes up novels and songs or the tools that make up dramas and movies are extremely difficult or expensive, then it cannot become an art enjoyed by the general public; nor is it something we should praise.

Fifth, any sound era's artistic product should not have an erroneous performance of any social problem in the era. If we find incorrect explanations of women in novels, movies, dramas, and songs, we can devalue their prices.

Women's Issues Lecture

Section 2 From Female Superiority to Male Superiority 196

— Junhui

The phenomenon of female superiority is not limited to single-celled organisms; it also exists in most invertebrate animals. For example, among spiders, the larger female spider captures and eats the smaller male spider immediately after mating. Bees are a clear example of a female-centric society: male drones are smaller than female worker bees by a third and are far fewer in number. Besides performing the mating task, they only eat honey and do no work. Therefore, beekeepers often kill them!

That being said, the males of many creatures have now evolved to be on par with females, especially in higher animals such as birds and mammals, even humans, where males are stronger and more beautiful than females. What is the reason for this?

Originally, the sole task of the male was mating, so it was endowed with active and intense sexual desire. It constantly pursues females to provide new genetic elements. However, the female is the root of the species, with the task of preserving and reproducing the species. Therefore, in the male's competitive pursuit, she calmly chooses the male that is beneficial to her species as her mate. This selective mind is a unique instinct of females, completely different from male sexual desire. This female selection has led to jealousy among males, and even more intense competition, which necessitates their physical strength and beauty. It can be said that the reason why the bodies of most higher animals, even human males, are so strong and beautiful is the result of female selection. At the same time, it is also the reason for the history of male evolution from an amorphous testicle to a one-jin head.

However, in the general animal kingdom, this so-called male superiority does not mean male dominance. For example, the peacock's elegance and strength are not meant to dominate females; on the contrary, they are meant to win the selection of the female peacock. That is to say, the female peacock still retains her right to choose. The female remains the dominant one.

We often hear the following arguments for male superiority:

'Men's brains weigh one jin, while women's brains weigh eight liang.'

'Men can kill cattle, while women can only kill chickens!'

These are undeniable facts, but Mr. Walter, the author of the female-centric theory, also tells us the following more accurate facts:

'The female is the root of the organism, and the male is a derivative.'

'The most primitive male is an amorphous testicle, a small worm with only reproductive organs and no nutritional organs!'

If both of the above are true, then the current male with a one-jin brain must undoubtedly have evolved from 'an amorphous testicle.' But how can an amorphous testicle transform into a manly man with a one-jin brain? This is a very interesting question, and our task is to investigate this mysterious evolutionary process of men.

Walter's female-centric theory correctly solves the problem of the superiority of men and women in biology. According to his research, all organisms have the sole and absolute task of species reproduction, species preservation, and species propagation, and the executor of this task is the female. Therefore, it is said that the female is the root of the organism.

Originally, the reproduction of organisms does not necessarily require the existence of males. That is to say, in the biological world, in addition to sexual reproduction, there is also a wide range of asexual reproduction methods. For example, so-called fission reproduction, budding reproduction, spore budding reproduction, and spore reproduction do not involve fertilization. Although these asexual reproduction methods do not distinguish between males and females, biologists commonly determine the female based on the producer of offspring. For example, in the case of fission reproduction, the terms 'mother cell' and 'daughter cell' are often used. From this perspective, organisms can reproduce without males. But why did males emerge to take on the task of fertilization? The reason is simple: life not only needs an increase in quantity but also needs a qualitative improvement in vitality. To continue its prototype and to obtain beneficial changes in its organization, vitality is leaping in all directions. Due to the law of survival of the fittest, the beneficial method of so-called fertilization was discovered. Fertilization is nothing more than using the mixture of dissimilar substances to develop the individual's life to a higher stage. Thus, male fertilization is not a fundamental necessity for reproduction but a secondary method that arises for the beneficial evolution of organisms. In reality, the number of organisms that practice sexual reproduction is less than half of all organisms.

As mentioned above, males are something derived mid-way, and the meaning of their occurrence and existence lies entirely in performing the task of fertilization. Therefore, in some lower organisms, the entire body of the male consists of testicles, with no nutritional organs and no ability to survive on its own. It dies after completing the fertilization task. In some parasites, the female is thousands of times larger than the male. In humans, the female egg is three thousand times larger than the male sperm. Let's look at an interesting discovery by Darwin. He said, 'Barnacles are only female, but the two shells that bear them have two small pouches, each containing a small husband. Even more interesting are hermaphroditic barnacles, which, although they themselves possess both sexes, also carry several spare little husbands, even up to seven little husbands!'

The Life of Women in Italy 197

— (Italian Correspondence) (Wanfang)

Under the slogan of 'Women return to the home, work is left for men to do,' what the actual life of Italian women is like is worth introducing to us.

There are currently more than 1.13 million registered unemployed workers in Italy, of which women account for about 241,000. However, these are mostly official statistics. The actual number of unemployed people is much higher than the numbers above. The number of unemployed women is especially high.

In order to carry out the anti-factory employment of women movement, the Italian government is currently engaged in the following work: (1) Reducing the value of women's labor and reducing wages to the smallest possible amount; (2) Placing the burden of unemployment on the shoulders of women, because unemployed women are not entitled to any benefits according to the rules.

The wages of female rice harvesters (more than 180,000 female agricultural workers only do seasonal work) have been reduced from 25 lira (Italian currency) in 1925 to 9.60 lira (1933). In southern Italy, the wages of female agricultural workers have been reduced to only two and a half lira a day! (To let readers know the real value of Italian wages, it should be compared to the fact that a kilogram of bread costs one and a half to 1.90 lira.) These are still the formal wage reductions in the pan-fascist wage contracts. In reality, the degree of wage reduction is much lower than mentioned above.

In addition, the wages of working women are constantly being reduced because the wage contracts already contain several rules that allow employers to exploit them as much as possible. For example, the wage contract in the textile industry (the textile industry employs most of the workers in Italy—600,000) stipulates that wages can be reduced by 25%—50%, stipulates that there can be compensation for progress in weaving (obtained from reducing the wages of female workers), and finally, stipulates that the wages of young workers, who make up the majority in factories, cannot exceed 60% of the wages of adult workers.

In their difficult lives, some have courage. For example, in the Asiya Ge area, women and their children organized a demonstration against the forced membership of workers in the pan-fascist party.

In the You Ting area, a large group of women went to the mayor to demonstrate because their right to relief was deprived. Many leaflets had been distributed beforehand. Although there were heavy police guards, the demonstration was finally successful, and their demands were victorious.

Interview with Mr. Yu Qingtang 198

— Wu

Everyone who has lived in academic circles must know of a person named Yu Qingtang.

Mr. Yu is one of the earliest promoters of mass education in China, and also a prominent scholar. For several years, she has been diligently working on her educational work. Her stories are practical and down-to-earth. She is not like the so-called women's movement leaders who like to boast, sing high-sounding tunes, and shout slogans... This is also well-known to her friends.

This time, because the Women's Education Center on Hualong Road in this city opened, she rarely made the effort to come and attend in person, despite the long distance. Therefore, the reporter made a special trip to interview her for three minutes.

That day, Mr. Yu was wearing a light gray cloth robe, and outside, a bean-colored woolen coat. She looked very simple and sincere.

After the reporter waited for her to finish speaking on the stage, I went over to tell her my intention, and with her permission, we had the following pleasant conversation.

'Mr. Yu, what is your opinion on the issue of 'women should return to the home'?'

'My personal opinion on this issue is this: Women are also citizens of the country, just like men. Women must not give up their responsibility to the country and return to the home to do trivial things—in fact, after the industrial revolution, a large number of women have already been forced by life to participate in social production activities. It is impossible to go back. So, I always feel that Mussolini's opinion is a bit too extreme.'

'What about the recently debated hair-growing issue?'

'This is a very small issue.' Mr. Yu couldn't help but laugh. 'In any case, I think this is a freedom that everyone should have. There are many, many big problems in China today that urgently need to be solved by the authorities. The authorities don't need to worry about such small things.'

'Mr. Yu, what do you think should be the future direction of women's education in China?'

'Women's education is the same as everything in the entire education issue. It is also regulated by the social environment. Therefore, it seems very difficult to find a path for women's education alone. Assuming that the entire education issue can be solved one day, then women's education will naturally no longer be a problem. So, the current effort should still be based on solving the entire education issue as a prerequisite.'

At this time, someone from the Women's Education Center came to discuss other matters with her again. The reporter felt it was inconvenient to worry her any longer, so I bid farewell and left.

The Life of a Widow's Hall 199

— Qian

Several years ago, I visited a widow's hall. This widow's hall was an affiliated business of a charitable hall. The buildings were built in the courtyard of the charitable hall. The main entrance opened into the inner courtyard of the charitable hall, but this main entrance should not be opened, and it could not be heard three or five times a year. This not only showed that the widows living in the hall could not go out, but also guaranteed that they would not have extra-curricular activities. On each side of the wall on both sides of the door, there was a round hole with a diameter of more than two feet. A rotating barrel with a side opening was installed in the hole. The barrel could not only hold things, but also seat a twelve- or thirteen-year-old child. If something happened, the widows trapped inside the door only needed to turn the barrel with their hands. The door of the barrel would appear, and the objects or children would be placed in the barrel. Then, the barrel would be turned again, and the door of the barrel would appear in the outer inner courtyard. Therefore, these two rotating barrels were the main traffic routes for the widows in the hall to transmit messages and communicate with the outside world. As for the inner letter rooms, they were buildings connected one after another, with board walls at the bottom. Each room had a number, and each number lived in a family.

Although the widows living in the hall were complicated, we can roughly divide them into two types based on their motives for entering the hall: one is to solve non-life problems, and the other is to seek fame. Because once a widow enters the hall, in addition to the monthly money issued by the charitable hall to solve her own life problems, her son can live inside until he is two or three years old, and her daughter can live until the day she gets married. Each child can also receive half of the adult's monthly money inside, and the children can also go to the charitable hall's free school to study. Isn't this equivalent to solving the entire burden of life?

As for the second type of people who seek fame, they are of course widows from wealthy families. Their motives for entering the hall can be roughly divided into three: first, those wealthy families who have plenty of food and clothing have a young widow gathering at home. Needless to say, the honest ones, if they are a bit coquettish and cunning, will become a great concern for both the mother-in-law's family. As a result, everyone can only try their best to find a way to get her into the hall. In this way, not only will there be no scandals, but it will also be a matter of reputation among the villagers. Second, some young widows want to get out of this family prison by entering the hall because the husband's family is large, the population is large, and the family rules are strict. Third, some female sages who live in this world but have ancient hearts are entering the hall to preserve their chastity and pass on their fame for generations.

In addition, I also want to talk about the life in the hall and the current rules and procedures for entering the hall.

Widows can only be released outside twice a year, with a term of five to seven days each time, except for special accidents that require leave - which is very difficult to approve. These two times are the Qingming Festival in March to sweep the tombs and the Zhongyuan Festival in July to worship the ancestors. Their daily life in the hall is quite free. The food is taken care of by each person, and each family takes care of its own. Water is supplied by the public. There are two female servants in charge of purchasing and selling goods for the public. There are rich and poor people in the hall, so their lives are also different. In addition to making clothes and shoes for themselves and their children, poor widows mostly take on outside work, such as making shoe flowers, sewing clothes, embroidery, sewing sheep dung heads, drawing whips, and other light handiwork. What about the rich widows? Everything they should do themselves can be done by paying poor widows to do it, and they always want to secretly play cards.

When it comes to the rules and procedures for entering the hall, in addition to the express provision that the age must be below 30 - that is, the younger, the more qualified - the rest is difficult to say. Because on the one hand, it is not like a school recruiting students, posting advertisements and brochures, and outsiders have no way of knowing. On the other hand, it seems that nine out of ten people who have entered the hall are illegal. Because we know that the reason for establishing the widow's hall is nothing more than the good intentions of gentlemen to 'maintain morality' and 'care for widows'. However, in fact, none of the women who can enter the widow's hall do not have a deep relationship with the head of the charitable hall (general manager) or the big donors. It is even easier for rich people to enter the hall. As long as they immediately donate hundreds or thousands of dollars. The gate of the widow's hall is tightly closed to young widows who are truly poor and helpless!

Speaking of this, we want to ask young widows who are truly poor and helpless, if the gate of the widow's hall is open to them, is it possible for them to maintain their chastity? Under this transactional marriage system, the general situation of Chinese society, no matter which village or town, if there is a young widow in a poor family, the mother-in-law, uncle, or sister-in-law, nine out of ten of them will try their best to remarry (that is, resell) the poor widow. Even if the widow herself is willing to keep her chastity, it is impossible. Mr. Lu Xun clearly expresses this situation in his novel Blessing. When Mrs. Si heard that Xiang Lin's wife was forced by her mother-in-law to marry out in shame, she said in surprise;

'Oh, such a mother-in-law!' However, the old woman Wei replied

'Oh, my lady! You are really too big a household, what is this considered among us mountain people? She has a younger son, who also has to marry a wife. If she marries her, there will be this sum of money to use as betrothal gifts?' Therefore, being a chaste woman and keeping a widow is not something that everyone can do.
