Shenbao This City Supplement Amateur Weekly

Amateur Chat

Talking About Economic Principles 200

— Song Xudong

The 'economic principle' mentioned here does not refer to the general principles in economics, but to the lawful principles of simplification, saving, and convenience. This term 'economic principle' is known to anyone who has studied a little philosophy as Mach's so-called new invention. In Mach's philosophy, the original meaning of 'economic principle' is that all knowledge, concepts, and knowledge of objective things can only be attributed to the synthesis of subjective sensory elements. It is not an objective reflection, and the possibility and opening form of this sensory element and its synthesis are innate principles pre-existing in sensation and experience. Our knowledge and knowledge can only be obtained and absorbed based on these prior world elements, and can only be based on it. There is no so-called external world, objective, in its view, and it does not know. This means that in recognizing this matter, only sensory awareness is the only existence. All complex external worlds can be economically reduced to the synthesis of unique subjective sensory awareness, and the synthesis of this sensory awareness can be economically reduced to prior world elements or principles. How simple, economical, and convenient is this! Although Mr. Wang Xinggong praised him in his Methodology of Science, saying that "We study science to obtain the effect of thought. Mach regards thinking economy as the only duty of science, which is indeed insightful remarks." But we feel that Mr. Wang not only did not see the idealism and fideism of Mach's philosophy, but also equated Mach's economic principle with the intellectual economy in science. This may be a mistake! We also feel that in the process of human cultural progress, there is indeed a so-called economic principle, but it is something that has nothing to do with Mach's so-called economic principle. Because the former is metaphysics or even fideism, while the latter is scientific.

The development of human knowledge, its certain knowledge system and laws, before its formation, requires the efforts of many people to succeed. Not only in terms of number, a law must go through countless practitioners, countless scholars, intentionally or unintentionally, from the infinite complexity of facts, to experience, observe, think, and experiment, in order to extract a principle and set it as a law, but also in terms of time, it often takes many times, either short or long. For example, from the simple fact of heat generation by friction, it is possible to derive the law that heat is a kind of motion and energy conversion and non-reduction, but from the barbarians who knew to use wood or stone to generate heat by friction to get fire, they could not draw this scientific conclusion. Moreover, even after the Renaissance, when science had begun to flourish, the theory of phlogiston or caloric was still prevalent in the 18th century. Only until the 19th century did many scholars constantly experience, observe, think, and experiment, knowing that heat is a kind of molecular motion, knowing that the mechanical motion of friction can be converted into heat, and that the motion energy of friction is not lost in vain, but is transformed into heat energy. In this way, we can know how uneconomical thinking and labor are wasted in the formation of a principle or law. However, in the uneconomical efforts of the predecessors, a knowledge system, a principle or law, was obtained and passed on to future generations. Therefore, in the continuous exploration of the objective world, future generations do not need to go back to groping around blindly, and go back to repeating the experience, observation, thinking, and experimentation of the facts already included in this principle or law. Instead, they can directly adopt the principle or law to regulate new materials and facts, and move towards the path of new truths. In this way, we can truly say that this is a true principle of intellectual economy, because it can indeed make us economize thinking, economize labor, and economize time. For example, in the calculation of circumference and sphere, after knowing that the constant of π is equal to 3.1416, when calculating any circumference and sphere, we only need to substitute this constant.

Page 20

That is, there is no need to calculate it again. Other examples include the gas pressure law formula in physics, the law of universal gravitation, atomic weight in chemistry, natural selection and survival of the fittest in biology, and the materialistic historical laws in sociology. As long as we know them once, when we need them in the future, we don't need to repeat the calculation, investigation, reasoning, and comparison from each event. We can easily and economically use it to explore and discover new truths. Science is the entire legacy of human knowledge. It can enable future generations who inherit this legacy to economize their thinking and labor in continued research. Scientific laws are the economic principles of human thought.

Not only is there such an economic principle in thought, but also in the process of human production and material life, there is also this economic principle; all inventions from ancient humans to the present are economic principles that can save our labor when we fight against nature and overcome nature. Because if we cannot use the inventions of our predecessors, and have to invent things ourselves to deal with nature, it will not only cost too much effort, but also will not be able to achieve large-scale results. The predecessors invented fire, which can enable us later generations to easily soften and cook rice and vegetables, and soften iron for easy manufacturing; the predecessors invented boats, which can enable us to cross rivers and seas without effort. Otherwise, we would have to spend more energy and time chewing when we eat, and we would have to waste a lot of time and energy to grind raw iron into tools. It would be almost impossible for us to swim across large rivers and seas. Modern people have invented machines to replace manpower. The ease and rapid effectiveness of single planting and saving do not know how much physical strength we have saved in production. What is this if not the economic principle? If we go further, the development of science and production, which is the speed of nature, time and space, allows us to economically use it through the gifts of our predecessors. Before there were steamships, trains, and airplanes, the matter of going around the earth once seemed to us a very large space, but now we are equal to shortening and shrinking it, and we can economically pass through this space within a week. In terms of time, it probably took several years to walk in the past, but now it can be done in a week. Telescopes make planets that are hundreds of millions of miles away seem to be right in front of you for you to observe. Wireless telegraphs and wired telegraphs can allow you to receive news tens of thousands of miles away in a few hours. Isn't this time and space being economically used by people?

In short, the development of science and the progress of human production are all about making our lives and thinking economical and simple. This is the economic principle of science, not the metaphysical economic principle of Mach. Humans are pushed forward in this economic principle, and culture can only develop in this economic principle. Without the effect of this economic principle, humans would still be in the barbaric stage, unable to have much thought and rich lives. Therefore, both spiritual and material civilization originate from this economic principle.

Confessions of a Career Woman

Bleached Bones 201

— Recorded by Ms. Juan

Female Fortune Teller, Hongmei, Speaks

I was born nineteen years ago, in a spring, into a "respected family" of Wu Shu in Changhong. On the day I was born, the whole family was filled with an indescribable joy. Although the idea of valuing boys over girls was still deeply rooted in our family, I was my father's only daughter after seven years of marriage, so they couldn't help but make a fuss over me.

My father was a simple and honest middle-aged man, and his life could be described as peacefully living a plain life. All the internal and external affairs of the family were handled solely by my mother. Although my mother was a woman with outdated ideas, her knowledge, experience, and worldly wisdom were much higher than my father's. A family of thirty people, all income and expenses, were all under my mother's control. It must be said that this required considerable talent.

I grew up in such a family environment, and the happiness I enjoyed at that time was indeed something I cannot express in words now. My father was willing to not ask about family matters, but he would never neglect my living environment. In his daily life, he spent a small portion of his time reading, and the rest was almost entirely spent playing and laughing with me. I can say that my father's life had no wild celebrations, nor did it have any worries.

My father abandoned his wife and daughter and left this world on a winter night. At that time, I was only a six-year-old child. Seeing my father's stiff body, I didn't feel any sadness at all. Later, seeing the mourning of relatives, it aroused my tears.

Since experiencing this excessive grief, my mother's body gradually weakened. Before, her love for me seemed very faint on the surface because my father was by my side all day. But after my father passed away, she loved me even more than when my father was alive. She didn't allow me to be apart from her for even a minute, and she wanted to bring me by her side for almost everything. In those two years, my nature gradually changed from innocent and charming to weak and shy.

The family situation deteriorated day by day, as if the god of happiness had died with my father. When my father passed away, all the funeral expenses were sustained by selling dozens of acres of land. In the following years, misfortune came one after another, and my family's fields were transferred to new owners year by year. My mother, in this environment of losing her husband, her young daughter, and the dissipation of her family property, her flesh and blood body withered away day by day like an oil lamp.

The day my mother's life ended was when the people of the entire city of Wuchang were making their final struggle with death. The warlords in the city were still stubbornly resisting the righteous revolutionary army outside the city. The intense artillery fire from both sides... constantly... There were always a few that landed on the edge of my house.

After dozens of days of fierce warfare with flying flesh and blood, the gates of Wuchang finally opened. After this unprecedented catastrophe, the scene in the city was as desolate as if it had been washed by water. People's faces were covered with a veil of excessive hunger, and they were taking their wives and children to leave this harsh environment one after another.

In that group after group of fleeing people, there was also a small life. At that time, the person who walked out died miserably, and now they have entered another world.

The misery that the past ten years have given me could have been avoided, but when faced with the reality of today, I can't help but be touched by the sweet illusions of my childhood life!

The fact that I embarked on this path of life in the world now seems like a dream. I remember that I started learning "the art of judging people" from Mr. Lingqing in the sixteenth year of the Republic of China. The person who introduced me was the one who brought me out of Wuchang. On the day I became an apprentice, I was still an eleven-year-old child. At that time, not to mention not understanding what learning "the art of judging people" was all about, even daily life like eating and dressing was still taken care of by Mr. Qing.

Because Mr. Qing did not have children of his own, I was able to enjoy the treatment of a daughter while being a student. She cherished me as much as if she had raised me herself, and she educated me, creating the foundation for me to learn "the art of judging people."

I started "practicing my art" since the year before last. In these two years, since I opened shop and became famous, more and more people have come to me for fortune-telling every day. From ten o'clock in the morning to twelve o'clock at night, I rarely have a chance to rest. In the twelve hours of fortune-telling time each day, there are probably more than ten customers. Among these many customers...

Page 21

...Of course, there are many who come with difficult questions seeking a resolution, but there are also those who have ulterior motives under the guise of fortune-telling.

Speaking of this fortune-telling profession, people who don't understand the inside story generally think of it as a free life with abundant income. But the hardship of the dark side is something that people wouldn't believe even if you told them. Especially when it comes to our income, that is an issue that gives everyone a headache. The price for one fortune-telling session is two yuan. If you have ten customers a day, you'll have an income of twenty yuan. This is naturally a rare reward in general women's professions. But while our income is large, our expenses are also considerable. The hotel room costs two yuan a day, and there are also advertising, leaflets, and living expenses, which cost at least ten yuan a day. When it comes to the end of the month, sometimes there isn't even ten yuan left over.

Speaking of the issue of placing advertisements, it reminds me of an interesting incident. Once, after my photo advertisement was published in the Shen Xin newspapers, many people called me the next day to ask why I published my photo at the same time as the advertisement. I hesitated for a long time about this question, and finally answered them like this: "I didn't have any other intention in publishing this photo. It's just that we are freelance professionals, and in order to make it easier for people to recognize us, I published the small photo along with it. If you must say there is another intention, then what about the many movie stars who provide their photos for people to sell for money?"

Those who called had nothing to say and hung up the phone. But in the following days, most of the young people who came to me for fortune-telling were "the drunkard's intention is not in the wine". My "Tai Xiansheng" turtle-fishing customer later replaced it with a different advertisement. That advertisement showed a human skeleton specimen, and below it was written: "No one likes this skeleton, but after an X-ray of Hongmei, it is no different from this skeleton. My ambition is to resolve people's fortunes and misfortunes, not to use my appearance as a deceptive facade..."

A few days after this advertisement was published, all the customers who came for fortune-telling were coming for fortune-telling. The experience that this fact gave me seems to make me feel that although this society is so cruel, as long as you have a method, you can still change it.

Life

Instructor 202

— Wu Lin

Because of a friend's introduction, I once worked as an instructor at the Shanzhou branch of the Longhai Railway Union in Shanzhou, western Henan. Before I "took office," I had seen the beautiful Western-style houses where the section chiefs and supervisors of the railway lived in Zhengzhou and Luoyang. I had also seen the not-so-bad meeting places of the railway unions in these places, so in my imagination, the Shanzhou branch's building would definitely not be too bad. However, when I arrived in Shanzhou and was led to the entrance of the union by a member of the branch's standing committee, I almost couldn't believe my eyes. The sign of the union was not hanging on a building, but on a rather large cave! I stood at the entrance of this cave, looked up, and, heavens, above the cave was a dirt cliff about ten feet high, with a large crack about three or four inches wide. It looked like it was about to collapse! I was stunned at that moment and didn't dare to go in, but the standing committee member said:

"This is the union, please come in!"

Since I was already here, what else could I do? I thought for a moment, then risked great danger and resolutely walked in.

You probably won't believe it, but in that cave, there was a large rectangular dining table, a first-class desk, and seven or eight chairs. The sloping walls on both sides were covered with things like "All under Heaven is for the Public" banners. The inner layer of the cave was the bedroom, with two beds. Although the entrance of the cave was not very wide, and there were certainly no windows on either side, the light was very sufficient. Even the inner layer of the cave was not very dark. If I hadn't seen from the outside that this was a cave, I would have thought it was a not-so-bad office of some kind.

The standing committee member and I sat down next to the dining table. A young errand boy, probably about twenty years old, poured two cups of tea. Then the standing committee member pointed to me and said to him:

"This is Instructor Zhang, specially sent by the general union. You must listen to his instructions in the future!"

After we talked about the situation of the union here, the standing committee member took his leave and left. Only the young errand boy and I were left here. Because the air was very quiet, it made me think of this cave again. I didn't know why the union wasn't set up in a building, but had to dig such a large cave to use as a meeting place. So I asked the young errand boy. According to him, this cave wasn't newly dug, but already had a history of three or four years. Most of the people here, outside of the station chiefs and supervisors on the railway outside the city, lived in such caves. It wasn't just the union that was set up in a cave. Moreover, this cave also had its special advantages, namely that it was warm in the winter and cool in the summer. So some people were even willing to live in a cave rather than in a house. This was indeed a strange story that I had never heard before.

At night, just as I was about to take off my clothes and go to sleep, I suddenly heard the sound of a whistle. A train was coming from the west, passing over the railway above the cave where I was staying. The entire cave shook, and the dirt from the top of the cave fell down with a rustling sound, scaring me out of my wits. I instinctively ran out, looking at the crack above the cave, which seemed to be gradually widening. "Oh no, it's about to collapse!" I couldn't help but shout. But the young errand boy laughed inside the cave, slowly came out, and said to me:

"Mr. Zhang, don't be afraid! The cave won't collapse. Look, aren't these people all living in caves?" He pointed at the people living on both sides of us.

The train had already passed, and the crack above the cave was still the same as before, and hadn't widened. It seemed like it wouldn't collapse immediately. So I calmed down and walked back in. Although my heart was still beating nervously, fearing that I would be buried alive in this cave tonight, since I was already here, what could I do? I had to resign myself to fate and stay here temporarily.

My salary was thirty-three yuan per month. Where did this money come from? It was quite embarrassing! All the union's expenses and my salary were paid by the workers. According to the general union's regulations, 1.5% of the workers' monthly income was extracted as expenses for each branch union. That is to say, a worker with a monthly salary of ten yuan had to take out fifteen cents for the union. Therefore, my main job was to urge the workers to pay their dues on time. In the first month or two after I arrived, it wasn't difficult to collect the dues. Once it was due, the workers from all over would pay the dues. But later, problems gradually arose. Some even didn't pay their dues for several months. For those workers who didn't pay their dues on time, I could still go to those nearby to ask for them. But there was no way to deal with the railway workers in places like Mianchi Guanyintang! They were one or two hundred miles away from Shanzhou, and I couldn't go to them to collect dues often. Therefore, later I just let it go, and those who really couldn't pay their dues were just counted as unpaid. Fortunately, the union's funds could still be maintained, and there wouldn't be too many problems.

Workers often had conflicts. As long as they couldn't resolve them privately, they would come to the cave to "file a complaint." This was the most difficult thing to handle. Because those workers were very straightforward, you couldn't use diplomatic means to say good things to both sides when commenting on their conflicts. That would make them say that you were weak and unfair. You had to clearly point out who was right and who was wrong for them to be convinced and say that you were fair and selfless. However, it wasn't easy to judge their right and wrong. If you made a mistake, you might even be scolded as a "confused idiot." However, I was still a "talented" person, and I handled several disputes between the workers without any major mistakes. So they treated me quite well. Whenever they had free time, they would run to the cave to talk to me about "Romance of the Three Kingdoms" and "Water Margin", chatting about this and that, or playing chess. Sometimes they would even invite me to drink a couple of glasses of baijiu and have a great time.

In this way, although I was living in a cave I had never lived in before, becoming a "cave-dwelling savage," I didn't feel lonely in life. The only thing that made people not very happy was that whenever a train passed over the cave, the cave would shake greatly, and the dirt on the top of the cave would fall down with a rustling sound, making you immediately feel the terror of "being buried alive in the cave." I remember that one night, it snowed heavily all night. When I got up the next morning, the snow outside the cave had accumulated one or two feet high, and the top of the cave was also covered with thick snow. The young errand boy went out to take a look for a while and said: "What heavy snow! When it snows heavily, the caves are dangerous! But our cave isn't afraid!..." "When it snows heavily, the caves are dangerous!" After hearing this warning, I couldn't help but feel a little nervous again. I thought, I haven't enjoyed the happiness of life yet, I haven't fulfilled my responsibility yet, if I were to be buried alive in this cave, it would be too unworthy. - The more I thought about it, the more terrified I became, the more panicked I became, as if the cave was about to collapse immediately. So I hurriedly packed my luggage and resolved to leave this dangerous place. When I was taking the train back east, I was still thinking in my heart: Has that cave collapsed? Has the young errand boy been buried alive? Are the people living in the caves there still safe?

Weekly Literary Society

Classicism in Literature 203

— Zhi Sheng

A segment of Chinese literary researchers have traditionally interpreted European literary trends in the past with a mistaken preconception. This preconception stands upon the position of formalism, relying on the terms "classical" and "romantic" to assume that "classical" possesses feudal characteristics and "romantic" represents the nature of the common people. Consequently, they argue that classicism reflects the consciousness of the feudal aristocracy, while romanticism signifies the literary trend of the emerging citizenry. Before 1930, this mistaken preconception resembled a self-evident truth. Whenever discussing past European literary trends, people would express this preconception in a formulaic manner, with few questioning it. It was only when Friche's "History of the Development of European Literature" was introduced to China that some individuals abandoned this erroneous preconception and embraced Friche's theory. However, many others stubbornly clung to this mistaken view. Not long ago, Mr. Ye Qing made an arbitrary claim in the inaugural issue of "World Literature" that classicism was feudalistic. This assertion was theoretically refuted, but no response has been seen to date. This is widely known. Yet, it is not surprising that someone like Mr. Ye would commit such an error. What is most astonishing is that some new literary researchers, theorists who guide young people in their study of literature, still operate under this preconception, asserting that classicism is feudal. For instance, in his "Two Different Romanticisms," Mr. Xin Ren, while accurately elucidating romanticism, still remains under the sway of this preconception...

Page 22

...stating that classicism is the "artistic form of the feudal system." Similarly, Mr. Yin Geng, in "Reading Life," not only claims that classicism is feudal but also asserts that "all previous eras were feudal societies" (see Mr. Yin Geng's "What to Write? How to Write?" in "Reading Life," volume one, issue seven). In light of these facts, we believe that it is still necessary to discuss what societal consciousness classicism represents.

First, when studying modern European literary trends, we must understand the Renaissance movement, as this movement emerged from the collapse of medieval feudal society and the development of commercial capitalism. To investigate the growth of the modern citizenry, one must understand the Renaissance movement, as it marks the beginning of the modern citizenry stepping onto the stage of history and striving to fulfill its historical tasks. Literature is a product of society, and the dominant and developing literary trend that appears in a particular era must reflect the consciousness of the dominant and progressing social stratum in that era. During the Renaissance, the medieval feudal society had collapsed, and the nature of society had become commercial capitalism. The commercial citizenry occupied a dominant position in all aspects, including culture. Therefore, the culture and literature of the Renaissance were those of commercial capitalism, not of feudalism. This culture and literature are the origins of modern culture and literature. It is no coincidence that scholars have traditionally begun their study of the development of modern civilization and modern literary trends from the Renaissance.

Classicism is a literary trend that arose with the Renaissance movement, triggered by the advancement of commercial capitalism. In fact, in 17th-century Europe, due to the development of commercial capitalism, the growing citizenry naturally strongly opposed the politically fragmented feudal system for the sake of trade convenience. What they urgently demanded was a strong, centralized political system. Consequently, absolute monarchical autocracies emerged in some European countries at that time. The demand of the growing citizenry, as reflected in literature, was an absolute classicism that valued reason, upheld discipline, opposed novelty, and depicted general human nature. Therefore, Friche believes that classicism reflects the worldview of the growing citizenry. The poet Boileau, in his "Art of Poetry," which is considered the "textbook of classicism," not only urges writers to "observe the nature of mankind with the eyes of reason" but also advocates respect for reality and truth, arguing that "there is no beauty outside of truth, only truth is worth loving." Such views are clearly not possessed by the theologically inclined, decadent feudal aristocracy but rather represent the consciousness of the growing citizenry. To say that classicism is a reflection of feudal consciousness is clearly a mistaken view that is inconsistent with the facts.

If we examine the societal consciousness expressed by several great classical writers in their works, the issue becomes even clearer. Corneille, the first classical writer, strove to attack feudal society and serve the growing citizenry. Racine was Corneille's successor and also a literary representative of the citizenry. Balzac, in his depiction of Roman citizens, even offered such praise: "He knows no national bonds, nor personal inclinations. He is devoid of vanity and greed. He would rather eliminate tyranny than share power with it. In him, there exists the courage of a hero, and on his face, there is stamped a great mark." Finally, there is Molière, the great creator of comedy, who in his plays worked to revive "the king who suppressed the powerful feudal lords." He depicted feudal nobles as "arrogant," "cold-blooded," "hypocritical," and "immoral" characters. He used the mouths of peasants to protest to the nobility, saying, "Do you think that just because you are a noble, you can freely seduce our wives in our place?" At the same time, he even used the servants of nobles to scold the nobles as dogs and demons. (Please refer to Chapter 3 of Friche's "History of the Development of European Literature.") Thus, if people cannot deny these facts, cannot deny that Corneille, Racine, Molière, and others expressed in their works the consciousness of the growing citizenry, which is not feudal thought, then to say that classicism is the "artistic form of the feudal system" is an irrational statement based on a misunderstanding of history.

Finally, we must especially draw people's attention to the social conditions and cultural situation of Europe after the Renaissance. We know that the European society after the Renaissance was a society in which commercial capitalism was developing. The cultural characteristics of this period were absolutism, humanism, naturalism, and classicism. Classicism is a combination of absolutism, humanism, and even naturalism. If classicism is said to be feudal, then absolutism, humanism, and even naturalism are also feudal. However, no scientific historian would regard absolutism, humanism, and naturalism after the Renaissance as feudal things. Naturally, the "citizenry" in our statement that classicism is a reflection of the worldview of the growing citizenry does not refer to existing entrepreneurs and bankers but rather to commercial citizens similar to those in the Greek and Roman eras but more advanced. However, regardless, commercial citizens are still citizens, and certainly not feudal lords. Therefore, the statement that classicism, which expresses the consciousness of commercial citizens, is feudal is still incorrect. At the same time, if we acknowledge that the commercial citizens of the Renaissance and later were more advanced than those of the Greek and Roman eras, then the classicism of the Renaissance and later, which reflected their worldview, was not simply a revival of classical literature from the Greek and Roman eras but a further development. It is the initial stage in the development process of modern civic literature. The reason why people regard classicism as a feudal literary trend is because they do not understand what the Renaissance was about, because they do not understand the European social conditions, cultural situation, and the essence of classicism after the Renaissance.

Book and Newspaper Introductions

After Reading "Modern" "Innovation Issue" 204

— Ou Renzheng

The recently published "Modern" Volume 6, Issue 2, in their own words, is a transformation from a literary magazine to a cultural magazine, and looking at the content of the entire magazine, it does indeed have the flavor of innovation. They are able to grasp the reader's heart, confidently offer commentary on reality, and provide easily understood explanations of profound theories that are generally desired by readers.

The short reviews in the "Modern Forum," such as Fuquan's "Handwriting Movement," "Sixty Percent Off Books" (This year is not the year of translation, it should be the year of sixty percent off), "Saving the Nation by Studying the Classics," and Shao Wen's "Why Are There No Great Critics in China Today? A Humorous Dead End," all grasp these important topics in the current cultural sphere and provide deep criticism.

In the political, economic, and cultural essays, Wei Ming's "From the Franco-Italian Compromise to the London Agreement" explains the process and content of these two major events and then discusses them, grasping the conclusion that the major European imperialist powers currently have a temporary and considerable reconciliation, which was successfully achieved under the unity of anti-Soviet Russia. Qian Zefu's "Characteristics of the Current Stage of World Economic Panic" points out that the so-called "improvement" in the current economic panic is only due to the development of "military industry," and the poverty of the people has not disappeared. Qi Qisheng's "The Core Problem of China's National Economic Development" is a review of the arguments of Independent Review. He criticizes the views of Tao Xisheng, Jing Chao, Liang Shuming, Gao Jian Si, and Zheng Linzhuang, considering their ideas as a tangled mess, and advocates taking rural revitalization as the core, but he only criticizes and has not yet presented his own concrete proposals. Fu Yisheng's "Where Is China's Publishing Industry Going?" analyzes China's publishing industry from the perspective of social changes and points out future trends.

In the "Popular Academic Lectures," Shao Wen's "The Value Problem of Literary Works" is, in my opinion, the best, and Wang Tefe's "The Worldview Derived from Electron Theory" is the most important. The former comprehensively discusses the relationship between content and form in the value of literary works, with clear analysis and thorough discussion. The latter, because in Chinese cultural circles, natural science is observed apart from society, now he actually integrates electron theory with worldview.

Several "Essays" allow readers to relax after reading some difficult essays, and the authors are also veteran writers such as Yu Dafu, Xu Weinan, Chen Zizhan, and Zhao Jingshen.

The handwriting vocabulary is the best arranged in this magazine. For example, "Taibai" arranges the vocabulary into two columns, which is very inconvenient to review. Here, it can be torn off and placed at hand for review.

Wang Jicong's "On Liang Shiqiu" in the "Writer Theory" is a strenuous essay. He peels Liang Shiqiu layer by layer, exposing what kind of thing the so-called humanism of Professor Liang and others is. But two photos of Liang Shiqiu and Babbitt are missing (because they pay close attention to illustrations, this is really indispensable here).

The two creations, Chen Shuxun, seem to belong to a new writer, but the "Tragedy of the Food Stall" published here also exposes the "chaotic change of occupation" of farmers and the continued lack of solutions after the chaotic change of occupation, and also writes about the injustice of the poor towards rent collectors, and says "I will fight you to the death." The technique is also very good, and he is a promising author.

Among the three "Book and Newspaper Reviews," Li Huaqing's "Introduction to Chinese University Student Diaries" has the least attention-grabbing title, but the content is worth noting. He is not introducing a book, but writing literary theory. Hui Xian's "Hu Translation of Pre-Qin Classics" is very enjoyable to read. It is a shame that the translator has such a thick skin to publish this kind of translation, and there will also be such an irresponsible publishing house to publish it.

The writers in "Women's Issues," Bi Yao and Bi Yun, seem to be female writers who often write for the "Female Voice" weekly and "Women's Garden." I think the issues they talk about should be more realistic. There are many realistic women's issues that need female writers to speak for themselves.

"Youth Life Guidance" has a very cautious attitude and is a very beneficial article for young students.

Cultural news is very rich, which is a small feature that can attract people to read.

But I have several dissatisfactions. (1) According to the "Innovation Issue" selling for three dimes, and the normal price being two dimes, the future length will be reduced by one-third. If this kind of comprehensive cultural magazine is reduced further, several parts will have to be reduced, which will inevitably disappoint readers. (2) The cover paper is too thin. Although it does not need to be as luxurious as "Human World," it must be thicker for preservation. (3) In terms of arrangement, it is too economical with paper. Each long article should start on a new page, and each column should start on a new page. Otherwise, it is too petty. To run a big magazine, you must have a big ambition. Readers will naturally flock to a magazine with such content. (4) In terms of content, there are still some important practical problems that the editors hope to pay attention to and present for discussion. I wonder if the editors and publishers of "Modern" can humbly accept my humble opinion?

A Week of Travel

The Holy Land of Confucius 205

— Chang Qing

When the train was just about to pass through the middle section, Qufu Station arrived. Tourists who are preparing to visit Qufu, when getting off at Qufu Station, usually first inquire: "Where are the Confucius Temple and the Confucius Cemetery?"

The Shandong locals will earnestly tell you: "Not here! It's still eighteen li away from here. Go east from the station, turn the corner, and you'll reach Qufu County, and you'll know."

We, who are new to Qufu, can be considered to have found the direction from here. We followed the local custom, walked east from the station to the main road, and each hired a sedan chair, with a fixed price of eighty cents. So the mules pulled the sedan chairs, bumping and shaking, driven by the coachmen. As we experienced this feudal style on the journey, we idealized the ancient scenery of the so-called Holy Land of Confucius even more. At this time, a strong anticipation arose in our minds, eagerly looking forward to admiring the scenery of the Holy Land. After passing through two villages, I shouted: "Ah! I can see it. At the edge of the distant woods, there are two yellow roofs. Among the green and dark villages, that solemn and grand building is revealed: this must be the Dacheng Hall of Qufu County, right?" I guessed while asking the coachman. The coachman said: "Yes, the yellow roof seen from here is the Dacheng Hall of the Confucius Temple. Those two large buildings were renovated by Zhang Zongchang at the expense of money. The one in the back is the shrine of Confucius' wife; the one in front is the Dacheng Hall."

Continued on page five

Page 23

The mule cart traveled quickly, and after advancing another village, we saw the city walls of Qufu again: in contrast, the magnificence of the Confucius Temple became more prominent. Just looking at the horizontal form of the city wall, one can deduce that Qufu is at least a first- or second-class county town. However, if you look down from the Dacheng Hall of the Confucius Temple, you can see at a glance that the entire Qufu county town seems to be decorated for the Confucius Temple. After the mule cart passed through another village, I asked the coachman again: 'Where is the Confucius Cemetery?' The coachman said: 'Hey! Haven't you seen it yet? Outside the city—outside the North Gate, that large forest garden two li away from here is it. Look at that very long wall! The tombs of the Confucius family from past dynasties are buried inside; Confucius' tomb is there and...it's worth a visit.'"

Bumping along the yellow earth road for about an hour. In an instant, our mule cart had arrived at the county seat. After entering the city and getting out of the car, we first went to the county government to visit a friend. At twelve o'clock, we went to visit the Confucius Temple together.

Coming out of the county government, passing through several winding street corners, the uneven streets end at the South Gate of Qufu County. Turning the corner from the South Gate, there is a flat lane, with a memorial archway erected in the middle with the words "Que Li" written on it. "Ah! This is Confucius' hometown! Are there any remaining historical sites now?" I asked. A friend who had lived in Qufu for many years said: "There's nothing much. Even the archway you just saw was built at the end of the Qing Dynasty. Going through the gate in front is the Confucius Temple." As he spoke, we walked into the gate of the Confucius Temple.

The Confucius Temple is grand and magnificent. There are many ancient trees inside, arranged around the overlapping and winding pavilions and corridors, which is indeed much greater than many other Confucian temples. From north to south, starting from the Dacheng Hall and ending at the gate, it divides the city of Qufu into east and west sections. There are many steles in the temple, mostly inscriptions left by emperors and famous scholars of past dynasties. In front of the Dacheng Hall is the "Apricot Altar" relic, which is a stone tablet, covered by a spacious pavilion, with an ancient tripod placed in front of it, surrounded by some ancient trees. Most of the people who visit this place like to take pictures here as a souvenir. In addition, what is especially worth remembering is the Dacheng Hall. The architecture of the Dacheng Hall is indeed magnificent, no less than the "Hall of Supreme Harmony" in the Qing Palace in Beijing. Inside the hall, there is only one Confucius statue, which is very solemn. On the left and right are ceremonial items and ancient musical instruments, covered with a thick layer of dust. Ten stone pillars carved with dragons are arranged in front of the hall, each with a diameter of more than three feet. The stone is fine and firm, and many tourists caress and embrace them, and their patterns and luster are also beautiful and lovely. It is said that Westerners once offered to buy them at a very high price, but were rejected by the descendants of Confucius, so they are still preserved to this day. This is certainly a valuable treasure with great artistic value in the Confucius Temple.

After visiting the Confucius Temple, we went out of the city to the Confucius Cemetery. The road from outside the North Gate to the Confucius Cemetery is very wide and neat, with ancient cypresses lined up along the way. There are even more trees in the Confucius Cemetery, but unfortunately, more than half of them have been cut down, and the newly planted ones have not yet become forests. It is said that due to the difficult lives of Confucius' descendants, they had no choice but to cut down a lot of them. The houses in the Confucius Cemetery are relatively simple. Inside, in addition to the overlapping and displayed inscriptions of past dynasties, there are relics of the elm tree planted by Zigong. This is a dry wood about ten feet high and about two feet thick, standing upright on the ground, covered with a small house, surrounded by glass, and you can look straight in from the window. People who don't know that it is a historical site often mistake it for a police guard post, thinking that the gardeners guarding the Confucius Cemetery are inside! Sigh! About a few hundred steps north of the cypress trees is Confucius' tomb. There is a simple stele in front of the tomb, but it has been weathered and cannot be seen clearly. The tomb mound is not very large, and blue trees and other miscellaneous trees are planted on all sides, and the tombs of Confucius' descendants are lined up in the vicinity, but they are all terribly desolate.

After visiting the Confucius Cemetery, we visited the Yansheng Duke Mansion next to the Confucius Temple with the introduction of the county government. The Yansheng Duke's name is Kong Decheng, and he is the 72nd generation descendant of Confucius.

We waited at the gate of the Duke Mansion for about twenty minutes before the receptionist of the Yansheng Duke Mansion came out to lead us to visit the Duke Mansion. In addition to the relics and items of the Kong family listed, we also took a walk in the garden. Although the rocks, flowers, and plants inside were good, it was a pity that they were not very neat. After looking around, I was led to sit down in the reception room. At this time, the Yansheng Duke was led out by his teacher. We saw that his demeanor was very solemn. It is said that he is not yet sixteen years old, but his demeanor is enough to show that he is knowledgeable and courteous. The friends who went to visit with us told us that the people of Qufu call him the "Living Sage." After the receptionist introduced us one by one, a friend began to ask the Yansheng Duke about his life and his interest in learning, but for some reason, he did not answer. However, immediately, the teacher who accompanied him spoke up and said: "The Yansheng Duke is currently in the period of studying, and I am afraid that he cannot answer the inquiries of the guests in detail. I can answer one or two as appropriate. In addition to reading the books of the sages, the Yansheng Duke also learns English, mathematics, physics, and chemistry. The Yansheng Duke is the main body in the mansion, and the management of finances is the responsibility of the steward; in addition, there are also special personnel responsible for medical care, teaching, and managing the Confucius Temple and the Confucius Cemetery..."

After exchanging greetings for a while, we said goodbye and left the Yansheng Duke Mansion. According to the locals: "The Kong family's land accounts for about three-quarters of Qufu County; although it is usually not subject to taxes, because the descendants of the Kong family do not care much about the industry, it is now difficult for many tenants to sort out the situation. Due to the same situation, the Yansheng Duke's finances are also very difficult. His entire property is not enough to supply the monthly expenses of the various department staff and the gardeners of the Confucius Temple and the Confucius Cemetery. People are worried: I don't know in which year the Kong family will have hope of prosperity (meaning to get rich)!"

Half an Hour at the Post Office 206

— Zhe

It was just after the first day of the month, and at 1:40 in the afternoon, I strolled into the Jing'an Temple Road Post Office.

As soon as I pushed open the heavy glass door, I heard a roaring sound and saw that the counter was crowded with people. I had just taken a spot when a pile of human flesh pressed against me from behind. What's the matter, why are so many people here today waiting to remit money?

To my right, two women were mumbling. One of them, with a face full of wrinkles, temples streaked with white, and a mouth like a sunken hole, had greasy white eye secretions stuck to the corners of her eyes. She pursed her lips and talked seriously to the other younger woman next to her, both speaking with an Anhui accent.

I finished writing the remittance form and rested my elbows on the counter, looking at the two women. I paid attention to their clothes and guessed that they were both honest and good people from the countryside. I don't know why, but the old woman also noticed me next to her, and it seemed that she knew from my clothes that I was still literate. Suddenly, a humble smile appeared on her wrinkled face, and she tremblingly held out her remittance form to me, saying respectfully:

"Sir," she nodded and smiled. "Please—oh, sir, this letter, oh, did Lao Huang write it from ×× Town, Wuwei County, Anhui...? Sorry, sir!"

The Lao Huang she was talking about was probably a colleague of the master she was working for as a domestic helper, or maybe the master's chauffeur, or something else. Maybe she had just gotten her wages yesterday and was sending it all home today. She didn't use a penny; her family was probably longing for Shanghai by the sea, hoping to have money sent back. The countryside was bankrupt, and this old woman had probably rushed to Shanghai because the countryside was bankrupt—I thought shyly, so I took her remittance form and envelope and read them. There was nothing wrong with what was written on it, it was "×× Store, ×× Town, Wuwei County—" but the name of the province was not written. I thought that maybe writing the name of the province would be clearer, so I asked her:

"Is Wuwei County in Anhui?"

"Yes, yes—" the old woman's face was full of respectful and humble smiles.

"Oh, then I'll add the words Anhui for you, it's not written Anhui above."

"Ah, did Lao Huang write it wrong? Ah ah, what's the matter, what's the matter, what should I do if it's wrong? Foreign money—" Her wrinkled face, which had lost its color, turned green in panic.

"It's not wrong, grandma, he's not wrong, Wuwei County is right, I said it would be clearer to add the word Anhui above." I smiled and immediately added the blue words "Anhui" at the top of the ink-written characters with a fountain pen. The onlookers burst into laughter.

She was grateful, tears welled up in her eyes, and she nodded, "Thank you, oh, sir, thank you, thank you."

She kept thanking me, and I was a little embarrassed. I didn't know why she was so grateful to me, I didn't give her any great favor.

People continued to come in from outside the glass window. Some just bought a few cents of stamps and left, and some went to the parcel counter to pack. Only the remittance counter was still crowded with people. According to the post office regulations, remittances would not begin until two o'clock, and there were still twenty minutes left. But it was already crowded at this time. The old woman muttered, and the gray wool hat was lying on the counter to write the money order. The blue-eyed foreign woman was speaking "Pidgin English" with the postal worker selling stamps.

The old woman showed the remittance form to the businessman-like person next to her again, and the old woman said:

"The kind sir just added it for me," she pointed to the blue words. "Sir, is this how it's written? Lao Huang is really confused, sir!"

The melon-skinned hat nodded a little, "That's right!"

So the old woman turned towards me again: "Sir, kind sir, thank you so much. Heh heh, sir, I still have a two-year-old grandson at home, you know, I wouldn't have bothered to come to Shanghai to work if I didn't have to, but, sir, sir, the mother of Xiao Sanzi, sir, my daughter-in-law, is strong and healthy, but she has to stay at home to take care of the children!"

She babbled on, telling her story, and I listened quietly to her story. My smile turned to seriousness, and a scene of a desolate countryside unfolded before my eyes. Those people were running around for a living, and I admired this old woman's "interest in life," and I grieved for the fate of this thin and frail old woman!

It was two o'clock, and the old woman handed two snow-white silver dollars to the postal worker, who dropped them into the drawer with a clang. The old woman took the slip of paper, stuffed it into an envelope, and walked out of the crowd with a happy face.

"Thank you, sir, oh, thank you, thank you!"

She thanked me like this again, and I couldn't think of anything to say to her, and I was very awkward. I also finished the remittance procedures and left the counter. It was 2:10 at this time. In half an hour at the post office, I took a course in sociology and a course in the philosophy of life.

Walking out of the heavy door, I saw the smiles floating on the bitter faces of those in a corner of a village in Anhui. I also saw my mother's smiling face, and I also saw countless countless starving eyes in the countryside looking up at the money flying to the seaside, but most of them were still recovering from disappointment with ugly bitter faces.

A string of tragic human heads rolling. My head was dizzy.

Biographies of Celebrities

The Biography of Einstein (7) 208

— From Mu

In 1914, there was a total solar eclipse near the German-Russian border that could be observed. At this time, Einstein hoped that his theory would be proven, but this year, due to the outbreak of the war, the German observation team became prisoners of Russia, and Einstein's opportunity was lost. The experiment at the Ritzke Observatory in 1918 also ended in failure. The British astronomer Eddington was a researcher of relativity. In 1917, he published his explanation; in March of the same year, at the proposal of the British Astroma and Royal, because of the total solar eclipse observation in May 1919, preparations were made at the joint meeting of the Royal Society and the Royal Astronomical Society, taking into account the results of the climate, it was decided to send observation teams to two places on the total solar eclipse line. Eddington participated in the African team. On the day of the solar eclipse, the African side was sunny, so they took several photos, which showed the existence of the Einstein effect. Another team also encountered sunny weather, and the results of the photography of the large and small telescopes there were credible on the small side, but also clearly verified the Einstein effect. The report at the joint meeting of the Royal Society and the Royal Astronomical Society in London on November 6, 1919, showed that Einstein's law was more proven than Newton's. (To be continued)

Radio Broadcast Programs

Special Programs 209

Storytelling 211

Jiang Ruting and Zhu Jiesheng, "Luo Jinshan"

Zhonghua (1140), 9:00 PM to 9:45 PM

Opening Passage "Ancient Tang"

There are myriad joyful things in the world, but the taste of romance is the sweetest. I advise people to indulge in prostitution, only to find themselves spending their fortunes in front of everyone. These pleasure-seeking libertines only need to sleep in a brothel once to feel like living immortals, as the saying goes. Where is the zither of Liu Xiahui after his death? The virtuous man has not been seen receiving incense. The ancients said that beauty is loved by everyone, and the immortal Lü Zu teased the peony three times. He has an immaculate heart of eighty-nine mysterious arts. The oil vendor runs a small business, grinding the mill with his feet and shoulders, exclusively favoring the courtesan, even paying extra. Zheng Yuanhe squandered his gold and silver and sold himself to Laixing, achieving the top scholar position through diligent study, but ultimately indebted to Li Yaxian. Do not regard gold and silver as precious as life. Tao Zhu's death leaves only empty fists. Only paper ashes are received before the spirit. Stealing half a day of leisure in fleeting life costs only a little flower powder money. The ancients said that romance is vast and boundless.

Yao Xiaoan, Wang Pingqiu, and Qilin Leopard

Zhongxi (1040), 11:00 PM to 12:00 PM

Opening Passage "West Lake Scene"

The West Lake scenery is truly extraordinary. The flowers on both banks are all unique. Let us all enjoy the road to Gushan together. The road out of Gushan leads to Bai Causeway. West of the causeway, Lingyin Temple and Yun Guang are remarkable. The carved beams and red lacquered doors of the temple face the high peaks of the South. From there, one can see the waters of the Qiantang River flying. Boats cross the three or five six bridges. After crossing the six bridges, the road is not lost. The most enchanting are the willows of Su Causeway, green willows and red peaches separated by bamboo fences. Next to the fence, one goes straight up Phoenix Ridge. At the ridge, there is Qingquan Creek with nine streams. The most famous on the creek is the Eighteen Creeks. The water flows strangely in the creeks, regardless of high or low steps. One walks towards Yue Fei's tomb with a heavy heart, feeling a sudden burst of anger, cursing the treacherous minister Qin Hui's wife. When the wife is not virtuous, the husband suffers misfortune. Misfortune arises unexpectedly and is difficult to escape. Leaving the body, one proceeds forward, reaching the lakeside and gazing around. One sees the wonderful scenery of the outer lake, the enchanting Three Pools Mirroring the Moon on the islet. On the islet, green moss is in the colors of spring. The beauties of the inner lake have fairylike faces. They slowly move along the Jade Belt Bridge. Shadows of flowers move as the setting sun shines, illuminating the seven-tiered pagoda of Leifeng. After climbing to the top, one looks far and sees the distant City God Temple and Tianzhu scenery vaguely. The scattered desolate village is in the setting sun.

Classical Prose 213

Wang Bingmei, Donglai Discussions

Huaxing (1260), 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Zang Xibo Advises Against Watching Fish

The way to remonstrate is not to make the ruler fear our words, but to make the ruler believe our words. To make the ruler believe our words, it is better to make the ruler enjoy our words. To warn with disaster is to make the ruler fear. To explain with reason is to make the ruler believe. To awaken with the heart is to make the ruler enjoy. Raising the chaos of the Tianbao era could not stop Emperor Jingzong's trip to Lishan. Raising the siege of the capital could not alleviate Emperor Xianzong's infatuation with the Buddha's bones. Was it not because they only warned with disaster and never explained with reason? Discussing the principles of court assemblies could not stop Duke Zhuang from watching the community sacrifice. Discussing the essence of pitch pipes and musical scales could not stop King Jing from casting bells. Was it not because they only explained with reason and never awakened with the heart? Disaster can indeed make people fear, but when encountering arrogance, our arguments are exhausted. Reason can indeed make people believe, but when encountering confusion and disbelief, our arguments are exhausted.

Shenbao Local Supplement Movie Special

Mourning Ms. Ruan Lingyu 214

— Reporter

We cannot but mourn Ms. Ruan Lingyu with the greatest grief, on this day of the March 8th International Women's Day of 1935, the one-year anniversary of Ai Xia's death, when we received the news of her death.

It is no exaggeration to say that Ms. Ruan Lingyu's death is not only a loss to her personally, nor to her family or a certain group of people who knew her, but a loss to the entire Chinese film industry. This is because she was a talented actress. From her first work at Lianhua Company, which was also the work that made her known to people, "Spring Dream in the Old Capital," to "Wild Grass Blossoms," "Love and Duty," "A Cut Plum Blossom," "The Plum Blossom's Tears of Blood," "Yu Tang Chun," "Sequel to Spring Dream in the Old Capital," "Three Modern Women," "Night in the City," "Little Toys," "Coming Home," "Life," "The Goddess," all the way to her last work, "New Woman" (and "National Customs" which was not finished), in terms of her acting skills, it can be said that there was not a single one that did not demonstrate her excellent acting skills. Of course, we do not want to review each of her works now, but generally speaking, she left behind many achievements for Chinese cinema. Especially in "Three Modern Women," which was the first Chinese film to enter a new stage, she played a role that she had no life experience in, and in "Night in the City," "The Goddess," and "New Woman," she demonstrated her unique talent. But now she is dead, and we can no longer see her new works. This talented actress with a great future! We cannot but lament the loss to Chinese cinema!

Because of her suicide, people will not forget that in "New Woman" she played the role of a woman from a small propertied class who committed suicide due to the contradiction between life and will, and the suffering given to her by society, thus cursing the "revelation" of suicide in "New Woman," which has bad incitement for her and for the whole society. At the same time, on the other hand, people will not ignore the lawsuits about damaging her reputation that have been published in various newspapers in recent days. But after we delve into "New Woman" for observation, "New Woman" is by no means an inspiration for women to commit suicide. On the contrary, the playwright is against suicide; this is revealed by the playwright's intention through the mouth of the female worker A Ying. Opposing suicide as the theme of the play is precisely one point of the playwright's success. At the same time, according to the reporter's investigation, Ruan Lingyu bought more than half a dozen sleeping pills long before the lawsuit occurred. At that time, the people of Lianhua Second Factory had notified Ms. Ruan's mother to keep a close watch, which is enough to prove that her suicide motive was definitely not recent. So why did Ruan Lingyu commit suicide? Was it the instigation of "New Woman"? Was it the reputational relationship of the divorce case? In addition to these two, is there the common economic relationship of suicide? From the point of view that she had a very high monthly income, it is of course impossible to be a reason.

Generally speaking, Chinese women in the current stage can feel great pain everywhere, making it possible for them to die tragically. Especially small propertied women, just as "New Woman" says, they struggle painfully in the contradiction between life and will every day. And more conscious women such as Ruan Lingyu, they want to climb up because of the temptation of material things, but in fact they are not allowed to do so easily. At the same time, they want to actively merge with the masses of production and embark on the road of resistance, but they know that they cannot stand that kind of cruel torment in life. They need spiritual improvement, but at the same time they also need life improvement, so this internal conflict and contradiction cannot be resolved, and suicide to destroy oneself in the contradiction is by no means an accidental result. Furthermore, many women regard marrying as a "destination," but after they marry, they cannot get sincere love and comfort, but only material anesthesia. As for Ms. Ruan personally, due to the records in the newspapers, she could not but suffer unbearable pain and stimulation, so although this was not her motive for suicide, it was also one of the main reasons for her suicide. In this way, Ms. Ruan is a courageous conscientious objector. For the seriousness of her own life, for the respect of her personality, for the disillusionment of spiritual improvement, and for the desire to get rid of pain and boredom, her suicide is a courageous expression for herself.

Yes, her suicide and Ms. Ai Xia's suicide are the expression of the distress of Chinese small propertied women. They are all conscientious and brave martyrs, but are suicides warriors? On the contrary, with the courage to commit suicide, what else is impossible to do? We firmly oppose suicide. We believe that the murderers of Ruan Lingyu are not certain individuals, let alone the instigation of "New Woman," but the real culprit is the evil society. Then, not being able to resist the evil forces of society, but becoming a victim of society, is a sign of weakness. Then, since she could not die for a noble cause, even if she knew after death, as "New Woman" says, she would regret it very much. At the same time, how weak is the significance of March 8th for Chinese women! Oh! This evil present society, may thousands of heroines transform the determination to commit suicide into revolutionary action for the common way out for oppressed women, and bravely avenge the sisters who have died! Because Ms. Ruan Lingyu died on March 8th, the reporter cannot but shout so boldly.

Movie Reviews

Review of "Racing Smiles" 215

— Jihan

6 Day Bike Rider Great Light

Not joking: because there are currently several new soft gentlemen who are emphasizing the artistic value of movies, that is, when they are demanding that movies appear completely as entertainment, if their theory can exist, I almost want to recommend the author of "Racing Smiles" as their standard mentor.

Isn't it? In this film, all there is are gimmicks, gimmicks, and the third is still gimmicks. Joe Brown's big mouth is so big that just this big mouth is enough to make you laugh. He used to ride a bicycle, riding very cleverly, like watching a bicycle performance in the Great World, which is enough to surprise people. And he can take off his clothes, take off his pants on the bike, the bike runs over banana peels, falls, and this makes the soft gentlemen crack their big mouths and laugh, like Joe Brown's. In short, this film can make people laugh, no matter how reluctant and stiff these gimmicks are, but the audience is laughing in the theater for a while. Then this is entertainment, this is the unprincipled artistic value required by the soft gentlemen.

But ah, if artistic value is only explained in this way, if the so-called artistic pleasure is just the stacking of stiff skills without content, then the art of film should really be destroyed from now on.

Everyone knows that without content, there is no form, and there is absolutely no artistic value based solely on skills. So what is the content of "Racing Smiles"? A young man, no matter how clumsy he is, as long as he is brave, he can always win the favor of a beauty. And that beauty is the daughter of a banker, of course, the son-in-law's fortune is not a problem. So in the end we see the young man walking happily with his lovely wife and children.

I think there is no need to explain it any further, it is so vulgar and empty, what else can we say? But the soft gentlemen say that content is secondary, and only ask for so-called pleasure. But the pleasure here will not leave any deep impression in the audience's memory, right?

Several Comedians on the Silver Screen 216

— Guangyi

Comedians are welcomed all over the world. Their art has no borders and is understood by everyone. Here I tell you the little history of several comedians you often see:

Laurel and Hardy - This pair of comedians are the most popular in recent years. They are an old partnership, and they have both feature films and short films, but most of them are short films. Laurel is British, born in 1895. He started acting on stage with his parents at the age of seven. He went to the United States at the age of sixteen and entered the Hollywood film industry at the age of twenty-three. Hardy is American, born in 1892, three years older than Laurel. Don't look down on him, he is actually a graduate of the Faculty of Law at the University of Georgia! He has had a special love for movies since early on, although he did not enter the film industry until he was twenty-two years old. The cooperation between Laurel and Hardy began with silent films. The films they co-star in now are all sound films, which are all laughable. Their recent work, "Toy World," has already been performed in Shanghai last month.

Charlie Chaplin - This is a well-known and most popular veteran comedian. He was born in London in 1889. His father was British and his mother was a dancer born in Spain. He lived in extreme poverty in his childhood. He served in the opera troupe at the age of eight. In 1906, he went to the United States with a British troupe. In 1913, he was promoted by the famous director Mack Sendett and entered the film industry. In the spring of 1931, he traveled to Europe. The French government specially awarded him an honorary military band. It is said that he will make a sound film after "City Lights."

Rock - Born in 1892 in Nebraska, USA, he was a famous comedian in his early years, but he has had very few works recently because he is already a wealthy millionaire. He apologized to our people for the anti-Chinese film "Fearless" he starred in, stating that it was a misunderstanding, and said that he admired Chinese cultural relics very much.

Pierce Caden - Born in Kansas, USA, he is famous for his facial expressions. Pierce's wife was originally a cousin of Noma Talmadge, but they later divorced due to discord, and married Ms. Mei, a nurse he met in the hospital while he was ill.

Will Rogers - A senior veteran in the film industry, born in 1879. After more than ten years of stage experience, he stepped into the film industry. He is not only a comedian, but also a writer and political commentator! He is currently the honorary mayor of Hollywood. He can get 125,000 gold yuan for each film he shoots. He has been to Shanghai and is an interesting typical American.

Ruan Lingyu's Spirit of Sacrifice is Unbearable to Recall 217

Although an artist's success requires talent, it also requires hard work and the courage to sacrifice the boundless hope of treasure. Like Ruan Lingyu, she was not only sincere and loyal to her work, but also did everything she could for the sacrifices that art required of her. During the filming of "New Woman," there was a scene where she had to roll down the staircase from the second floor. Director Cai intended to perform the scene with a long shot, and find someone with a similar figure to replace her falling. However, Ruan Lingyu thought that this would inevitably reduce the power of the drama. If the director agreed, she was willing to fall down the building herself to change the long shot to a medium shot. Of course, this was an unexpected gain that the director could not ask for. The result: it was so satisfactory, but Ruan's knees were broken.

Imperial Aunt Hu Shan Returns to the Silver Screen 218

Movie Queen Hu Die's beloved sister Hu Shan has not appeared on the silver screen for a long time. Those who do not know think that Hu Shan has left the silver screen life. In fact, Hu Shan is still determined to make progress in film art. It is said that Jixing Company's new film "Fang Yunying" is starred by Hu Shan. This drama depicts the life of artists, delicate and refined, artists strive for art and can not be tempted by profit and not be succumbed by power. Hu Shan plays the artist Fang Yunying, with expressions such as drama in the drama. The entire film has sound dialogues and singing. Photography and sound are handled by expert Johnson. The test screening was held at the company's studio yesterday, and the results were very perfect. It is said that it will be released at the Jincheng Grand Theater soon.

Movie Novel

Anecdotes of Wellington (The Iron Duke) (4) 219

— Xin Zhi

Louis, hearing this, finally sat down reassured and said, "Let's do it that way. Let's go to Ghent..." The Duchess, hearing this, immediately tried to stop him, but he kept grumbling, "Ugh... filthy hotels... we must stay... tasteless food... we must eat... dust... mud..." The Duchess, helpless, turned to the General in Southern Garb and said, "Capture him alive and hand him over to me." The General in Southern Garb bowed and said, "Certainly. Bring him back in an iron cage."

The General in Southern Garb led four thousand elite soldiers to meet Napoleon, but he did not capture Napoleon alive. Instead, Napoleon captured him alive. After being captured by Napoleon, the General in Southern Garb prostrated himself at the feet of his former master, offering him his life, his soldiers—everything. The soldiers' sense of obedience surpassed everything else. Before the General in Southern Garb left Paris, he was still a loyal subject of Louis XVIII, but Napoleon was his former master. The General in Southern Garb's example was followed by everyone in France. The entire country of France surrendered to Napoleon. In less than two weeks, Napoleon had entered Paris and once again became the Emperor of France.

At the headquarters in Brussels, the Duke of Wellington hastily reassembled the allied forces, already numbering over one thousand. At this time, Louis and his niece were living in Ghent, and his niece led the royal bodyguard to attack Paris every day. Wellington, hearing this news, rushed to Ghent overnight to see King Louis, telling him not to act rashly and informing him that Napoleon was currently at the height of his power and that even the allied forces were holding back, waiting for a good opportunity.

Wellington went to Ghent more than once, but every time he went to see Louis, the Duchess of Anorliet was always by his side, and she made no secret of her hostility towards Wellington.

A month, two months, three months passed in this way, and all of Europe was in a state of panic. The god of war descended upon the sky again, leering at the dead and wounded strewn across the battlefield, while funeral songs rose from all directions, echoed throughout the mountains and valleys. Napoleon's army set out, launching a swift and decisive attack on the allied forces, aiming to drive them out of French territory.

In the Brussels mansion of the Duchess of Richmond, the young and beautiful Duchess Frances Webster was helping the Duchess send out invitations. The Duchess was holding a dance party soon, and the Duchess was folding the invitations and putting them into envelopes for her. But her hands trembled, and nine times out of ten she couldn't get them in. The Duchess looked at her and said, "Frances, you're being more of a hindrance than a help. Just leave it to me." The Duchess sighed, "Charlotte, you can't blame me. Isn't he coming soon?"

The Duchess spat at her and said, "Tsk, you silly girl. The Duke of Wellington is coming to dinner. Why would he come so early?" The Duchess said, "Oh, I adore him..." The Duchess said, "But you've never even seen him." The Duchess said, "I have a portrait of him in my bedroom. His eyes—so handsome and lovely!" The Duchess asked, "Does your husband also think his eyes are handsome and lovely?" The Duchess said, "He's still in Constantinople." The Duchess said, "Is he going to be there forever?" The Duchess sighed again and said, "Charlotte, I beg you for one thing. When the Duke of Wellington arrives—please don't leave my side—or I might faint."

The Duchess was about to reply when suddenly there was a commotion upstairs, and the chandeliers above their heads shook. The Duchess couldn't help but cry out, "Oh no! I bet Wellington has arrived. He's playing with the children upstairs." As she said this, she immediately stood up and ran upstairs.

The noisy sounds in the room grew even louder. When the Duchess opened the door and entered, everyone was crawling on the floor. Besides the children, the Duke of Wellington, the one who had become the Iron Duke, was also crawling on the floor. The Duchess couldn't help but laugh and say, "If Bonaparte saw you like this, it wouldn't be bad." Wellington stood up and grinned, "That would be great. At least it might help him understand some sense of humor." (To be continued)
